Education Broadcast Special Issue

Trends in Normal School Education (Middle) 92

— Chang Daozhi, Director of the Department of Education, Central University

The modern teacher training institutions in our country can be traced back to the Regulations on Schools issued in the twenty-seventh year of Guangxu (1901 AD). Among them, normal schools "to train primary school teachers" were attached to middle schools, with a four-year study period. By the twenty-ninth year of Guangxu, the elementary normal schools in the Regulations on Schools were designated as independently established, with a five-year study period. In the first year of the Republic of China, the school system was revised, stipulating that the study period for normal schools was one year of preliminary training and four years of undergraduate studies, one year more than ordinary middle schools. Until the promulgation of the School System Reform Plan in the eleventh year of the Republic of China, our country's normal school system was largely modeled after Japan; normal school students' education began in elementary school, passed through higher elementary school, and then entered normal school. A detailed examination of this school system, directly imitated from Japan, actually takes the French system as its original model.

The current structure of the school system was completed in the School System Reform Plan of the eleventh year of the Republic of China. The organization of the primary and secondary school stages imitated the so-called six-three-three system in the United States; the duration of secondary education was extended, and the level of normal schools also increased accordingly. They were either established as normal departments of senior high schools or as six-year single-setting normal schools, but they could also be established independently for two or three years, accepting graduates from junior high schools (three or four years). After the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, there were no major changes in the school system. However, the Interim Regulations on Middle Schools promulgated by the University Council in March of the seventeenth year stipulated that senior high schools should have general, normal, and vocational departments, and the independently established normal schools lost their legal basis. It was not until the Normal School Law promulgated by the National Government in December of the twenty-first year that they regained their statutory independent status.

According to the current Normal School Law, normal schools accept junior high school graduates for a three-year study period and may also establish "special normal departments" for senior high school graduates for a one-year study period. The so-called special normal department is actually the second part of the regular department of the normal school in the school system of the early Republic of China, which was originally modeled after Japan. According to the current system, the level of normal schools is comparable to that of senior high schools, and senior high schools are evolved from higher schools and university preparatory courses. It can be seen that since the eleventh year of the Republic of China, the status of normal schools in the school system has obviously been raised compared to before, but it has always been confined to the secondary education stage. Its duration (including the combined number of years of prior education and normal education) is slightly longer than that of the Soviet Union, comparable to that of France and Italy, but it is already below the general standards of the United States, and it feels "far behind" compared to the training colleges in the United Kingdom. As for comparing it with the current German system of teacher colleges and the university training departments in the United Kingdom, it is even more beyond reach.

In addition, the current normal schools have added so-called simplified normal schools and simplified normal departments. The entrance qualification for the former is elementary school graduation, with a four-year study period, and the entrance qualification for the latter is junior high school graduation, with a one-year study period. Considering that modern teacher education in various countries strives to raise the level of education and enrich the content of training, this kind of simplified normal school seems to be only a temporary setting "for the sake of urgently training teachers for compulsory education."

Judging from the situation in all aspects, it is neither possible nor necessary to raise the level of normal schools in our country at present. Among the modern countries with the highest level of teacher education, the first is the United Kingdom and Germany. This is because the duration of their primary education is longer (5 to 14 years in the UK, 6 to 14 years in Germany), so their teachers need a longer period of preparation. Our primary schools are six years, and the compulsory education period is only four years; the teachers who will be needed the most in the future will naturally be for elementary schools, and the teachers trained by the current normal school system are already more than competent.

The United Kingdom and Germany have now implemented training elementary school teachers in universities or in independently established educational institutions at the university level. Education experts in France also advocate abolishing the current normal schools and having all future elementary school teachers receive one year of professional training in universities after completing full secondary school. The motivation for this kind of advocacy is only partly to broaden the knowledge of elementary school teachers; most of it is to raise the social status of elementary school teachers. In various countries, the demand to raise the status of teacher training institutions to the same level as universities mostly comes from the advocacy of education experts. Their intention is to break through the fortress of this traditional class education, correct the general prejudice that elementary school teachers are merely "teaching craftsmen," and advance them to the professional status similar to doctors, lawyers, and engineers. However, in our country, all primary schools from the beginning were not exclusively set up for the lower classes of society like European primary schools, so the teacher education system does not have the function of maintaining the current social class division. The normal school system in our country has similar points to the current French system on the surface, but it is actually different. Normal school students in our country generally need to go through the junior high school education stage, which is different from the fact that most French normal school students come from higher elementary schools and do not go through middle schools. Moreover, normal school students in our country have more opportunities to enter universities, so the normal education system itself is not completely isolated from the outside world, and it can avoid becoming the education institution of a certain specific class in society. This is a merit of the normal school system in our country that is worth preserving.

In the preceding paragraphs, I have given a general comparative explanation of the historical origins of teacher education, its social functions, and the teacher education systems of modern countries and our country. From the actual practice of teacher education in various countries, we can discover several key points that its entire spirit embodies. I will now describe them one by one as far as my personal views allow.

Teacher education from the beginning has been a powerful means to promote national cultural policy.

In European countries, the history of normal education is shorter than that of secondary and university education. When it was founded, it had clear national purposes. The French Revolution, launched in 1789, saw the importance of teacher education from the beginning by its revolutionary leaders. In 1794, it had already begun to create exemplary normal schools in Paris, ordering students to be selected from all over the country to enroll, so that in the future, each could return to their original place to run the same teacher training institutions. Napoleon had a deep understanding of the importance of teachers. In 1805, he said: "Education can be said to be the most important of all political issues; there can never be a stable political country without a group of professors who uphold definite beliefs." He had already seen clearly that the foundation of a nation-state lies in a common culture, a common belief, and a common ideal, and that teacher training is the root of everything.

After Prussia was conquered by Napoleon, its philosopher Fichte gave a "Speech to the German Nation" in Berlin in the seasons from 1807 to 1808. He believed that the key to the political regeneration of the German nation lies in moral and spiritual revival; he believed that a new generation of citizens must be cultivated through new education; this group of children should be allowed to run their own common life, completely isolated from adults except for a few teachers, so as not to be corrupted by their deeds. Although Fichte did not put forward a specific teacher training plan, the importance of teachers has been fully expressed in a few words. In the early nineteenth century, the Prussian government made extremely resolute efforts in teacher training. It is generally recognized that Prussia's establishment of teacher colleges created teachers who were thoroughly trained and full of professional enthusiasm, and they were worthy of being pioneers among modern countries. It is an unquestionable fact that the people trained by these teachers were the main force in the German national revival movement.

The normal schools in France were set up to cultivate citizens suitable for the new regime after the revolution, and the normal colleges in Germany were the creations in the movement to save the nation from danger; both are enough to show that the emergence of the modern teacher training system comes with great national purposes. If we only regard normal schools as places to train teachers, then we will have overlooked the greater significance!

Local News

Song Ziwen's Remarks Yesterday on the Sino-Japanese Problem: The Silence of the People Represents a Deep Understanding of the Government's Difficulties; Friendly Relations Should Not Be Discussed Before Relations are on the Right Track 93

Our reporter visited Song Ziwen, a standing committee member of the National Economic Council and chairman of the Bank of China, yesterday to inquire about the Bank of China's business situation last year and future plans. According to him, the Bank of China has a significant responsibility to society, considering the interests of the general public, and assisting the government in improving financial policies. Since taking office, he has been cautiously proceeding with this approach. Fortunately, thanks to the efforts of colleagues and the trust of society, deposits have increased significantly. The year-end settlement showed a surplus of four million yuan, with two million four hundred thousand yuan in official interest and over one million yuan in accumulated public reserve. New business plans for this year are currently under detailed discussion. He is currently preparing a detailed business report for last year to be presented at the shareholders' meeting this spring. When the reporter inquired about his views on the Sino-Japanese problem, Song replied that the recent tense pressure in North China has caused unbearable pain to our people. Except for the patriotic expressions of the young intellectual class, the rest remain silent. This is not the passive silence of the people, but a deep understanding of the government's difficulties. In the extremely dark situation in North China, they still hope to find a way to restore relations between the two countries to a normal track. Finally, the reporter asked about his thoughts on Sino-Japanese friendship. Song pondered for a moment and replied that when relations between the two countries have not yet entered a normal track, the word "friendship" seems rather difficult to explain. At this point, guests arrived one after another, and the reporter took his leave.

The Central, China and Communications Banks Sign a Contract with the Post Office: Methods for Exchanging Legal Tender 96

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Jiangwan branch office stating that the local post office was unwilling to exchange legal tender because it had not received orders from higher authorities, causing great inconvenience to merchants and residents who had only current currency. The Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Central Bank to negotiate. Yesterday, the Central Bank replied that the Central, China, and Communications Banks had signed a contract with the Directorate General of Posts, under which the three banks would regularly deposit legal tender in various post offices: 1,000 yuan in first-class post offices, 300 yuan in second-class post offices, and 150 yuan in third-class post offices. After the post offices exchanged for current currency, they could exchange legal tender with the banks in a cycle. The above methods will soon be implemented, and all legal tender exchange matters in the Jiangwan area can be resolved together.

The Money Trade Association Discussed the Year-End Closing Yesterday: Money Shops Begin Year-End Closing; Executive Committee to Meet Again on the 25th 99

The year-end closing period for all industries in the 24th year of the Republic of China is approaching rapidly. The money shops have begun to close their accounts. The Association held its seventh executive committee meeting of the third session yesterday. The details are as follows:

Start of Year-End Closing

After the money industry decided that January 23rd would be the year-end closing date for the 24th year of the Republic of China, the money shops began to handle the closing matters as the year-end closing period approached. They set a settlement date of the 15th for all customers, issued lists to each account, and extended the time for receiving and returning bills from the 19th. At the same time, they tightened up various loans, such as credit mortgages. The silver and money industries gradually became busy with collection and remittance. The internal office hours of the Money Industry Joint Reserve Treasury will be extended. Due to the consistent tightening by all shops, the Shanghai foreign exchange market still remained at eight points per thousand yuan per day in both the morning and afternoon sessions.

Executive Committee Meeting Held Yesterday

The Money Industry Association held its seventh executive committee meeting of the third session at 2:00 p.m. yesterday. Committee members Zhang Mengzhou, Liu Wuqiao, Yan Dayou, Wang Jiemei, Zhang Wenbo, and Shen Jingliang were present. Qin Xiqing, manager of the Joint Reserve Treasury, was also present. The meeting was chaired by He Zhongxiao, with Ge Huaiqing as the recorder. First, the chairman reported: 1. The resolutions of the last meeting; 2. Various reports on the Reserve Treasury. Items for discussion: 3. A letter from the Bo Mansion requesting a group greeting, stating that January 29th, which is the sixth day of the first lunar month, has been the annual group greeting event, usually held in the inner garden. This year, it is still planned to borrow the inner garden for one day. Please approve, etc. Should it be approved? It was resolved to approve the loan. 4. The date of the eighth executive committee meeting of the third session. It was resolved to hold it on January 25th, and the location was changed to the Money Industry Association Hall in the northern city, and a group greeting will be held. Finally, there was a mutual discussion on the matters to be prepared before the year-end closing. The meeting adjourned at 4:00 p.m.

The Central Mint Held a Meeting Yesterday: Approved New Coins and Factory Strips for December 101

The 29th Standing Committee Meeting of the Review Committee of the Central Mint was held at 4:30 p.m. yesterday in the conference room on the third floor of the Central Bank. Chaired by Chen Jian'an, the meeting approved over one million yuan of legal new coins and over two thousand factory strips. The meeting also reviewed the factory's accounts and work for December. It is heard that the factory has prepared a large quantity of subsidiary one-fen copper coins, which can be circulated after approval. The details are as follows:

Attending Committee Members

The committee members who attended the meeting yesterday included Chen Jian'an, Hao Shumin, Ya Jingchuiyi, Bei Songsheng, Ke Kebang, Song Hanzhang, Geng Aide, Lai Aisi, Qin Runqing, Yoshida Masatoshi, Hu Yunzhuang, Xue Laiton, Shi Huang, Xu Jilin, Hu Mengjia, Wu Yunzhai, Sato, Ma Xier, Xi Demao, Xu Mike, Lin Shu, and Ye Fuxiao, totaling twenty-two people. Also present were Director Chen Jian'an, Deputy Director Wei Xianzhang, Qiao Fusan, secretary of the Review Committee, Ge Laide, chemical tester, and Wang Depu, recorder. Chairman Kong Yongzhi was unable to attend due to business, and Committee Member Chen Jian'an acted as chairman.

Resolutions of Various Cases

The chairman announced the opening of the meeting and passed the minutes of the previous meeting. Secretary Qiao Fusan reported that 1,575,000 yuan of legal new coins and 2,861 Type B (880 fineness) factory strips had been reviewed and approved for release from the factory in December. They were listed, announced, and reported to the Ministry of Finance for record. The evaluation of factory affairs, review of factory accounts, and the work of the committee in December were also reported in detail. The chemical tester reported that the fineness and weight of the new coins produced in December were all within the legal tolerances, and that the Type B factory strips had also been stamped with the committee's seal in accordance with the regulations.

Minting Subsidiary Coins

The factory has been ordered to mint decimal subsidiary coins, and models have been ordered from abroad. After they were delivered, trial minting has begun. There are two types of copper coins, half a fen and one fen, and three types of nickel coins, five fen, one jiao, two jiao, and three jiao. After the subsidiary coin regulations are promulgated by the Legislative Yuan, they can be officially minted. It is now learned that a large quantity of one-fen copper subsidiary coins has been prepared. The obverse side is cast with the Kuomintang emblem of the blue sky and white sun, the reverse side is an ancient coin, with the words "one fen" on the left and right, and surrounded by a swastika pattern on all sides. After review, they can be circulated.

Attending Representatives

Chairman's Report

After the meeting began as scheduled, Chairman Wang Manyun reported, stating that Shanghai is the premier commercial port in East Asia, and various industries are very developed. However, the global economic downturn has affected the port, causing the market to decline and become depressed. The Shanghai Telephone Company, ignoring the market situation, is using the tool of communication to make arbitrary decisions as an enterprise. First, it used the excuse of losses to request a price increase, but failed. Then, it changed its approach, using the beautiful name of billing by call to achieve its purpose of increasing prices. In order to take into account the actual situation, the affordability of the citizens, and to restore the original prosperity, he hopes that all attendees will offer their opinions to find a solution. Society would be fortunate, and the citizens would be fortunate.

3. Regarding the issue of the special district telephone's disguised price increase, a serious expression should be made and a motion for reconsideration should be submitted. It was resolved to send letters to the Chinese and Foreign Ratepayers' Associations, convene a meeting of taxpayers, raise objections, and unanimously oppose it.

4. Regarding the case of sending letters to the exchanges, the hotel industry association, and other important users to contribute methods for collection, it was resolved to pass the motion.

5. Regarding the case of conducting a user survey, it was resolved to print forms and distribute them for completion.

6. Regarding the case of establishing a survey department due to the complexity of the survey work, it was resolved to pass the motion. The meeting adjourned at about 5:00 p.m.

Starting Today in the International Settlement, Opium Smokers Will Also Be Prosecuted: The Anti-Opium Regulations Will Not Be Applied for the Time Being 104

According to the Guomin News Agency, due to the agreement between the First Special District Court of this city and the concession, opium cases are still adjudicated according to the opium crime clauses of the Criminal Code. The Anti-Opium and Anti-Drug Regulations are ineffective in the concession. It is learned that Guo Yun'guan, President of the First Special District Court, has consulted with the concession authorities several times and has decided that from now on, when opium and drug cases are uncovered in the concession, the prosecution will be based on the Anti-Opium Regulations promulgated by the Director-General of Anti-Opium. However, the point in the regulations that opium and drug cases should be subject to military trial will not be applied in the concession for the time being. They must be handled as ordinary criminal cases according to the statutory procedures of the three-level three-trial system. It is also learned that the implementation date has been agreed upon by President Guo and the Public Works Department and will begin today (the 11th). Therefore, from now on, opium smokers residing in the International Settlement will also be severely punished if arrested.

Bureau of Social Affairs and Bureau of Public Health Yesterday Hosted Representatives from Designated Hospitals to Discuss Methods for Investigating Injured and Sick Workers, Aiming to Commence on February 1st 111

The Bureau of Social Affairs and the Bureau of Public Health, for the sake of protecting the health of laborers and promoting industrial economy, are jointly organizing a worker injury and illness investigation. To promote this effort, they specially hosted representatives from the designated hospitals of the bureau yesterday afternoon at the YMCA in Ba Xian Qiao, engaging in detailed discussions. Attendees included Zhang Ziyan from Shanghai Hospital, Shen Fusheng from the First and Second Hospitals of the Chinese Red Cross Society, Sheng Qingcheng from Hudong Hospital, Lu Yingen from Sacred Heart Hospital, Yan Peizhang from the Wusong District Health Office, Wang Shiwei from the Bureau of Public Health, and Tian Heqing, Wang Lianyu, Shen Risheng, and Jiang Zhiyong from the Bureau of Social Affairs. Chaired by Tian Heqing, the chairman first reported the purpose of the gathering, stating that the city has many factories, and many workers are injured or suffer from various occupational diseases due to their work in these factories. However, factories often conceal and fail to report such incidents, making investigations very difficult. In light of this, the bureau has drafted measures for investigating worker injuries and illnesses in order to promote this work. The measures are as follows:

* Select several larger hospitals in the city as designated hospitals to assist in this investigation.

* Invite those responsible for the designated hospitals to a tea party to discuss the implementation of the project together.

* Draft two report forms, one for "Worker Injury" and one for "Occupational Disease," to solicit opinions from those responsible for the hospitals and to determine the final form of the two tables.

* The above two record forms will be printed as postal card types and distributed to the designated hospitals and other major hospitals.

* Request each designated hospital to designate one person from its existing staff to be responsible for filling out the forms. If a worker is injured or ill and seeks treatment, the form should be filled out promptly and mailed to the bureau. If a worker is seriously injured, the Bureau of Social Affairs should be notified immediately by telephone so that staff can be dispatched to the factory for investigation.

* The bureau will provide appropriate remuneration to the form fillers mentioned above.

* The designated hospitals are tentatively set as follows: Shanghai Hospital, Binlong Hospital, Hudong Hospital, Renji Hospital, Guangci Hospital, Pudong Hospital, Wusong Health Practice Area, Sacred Heart Hospital, Orthopedic Hospital, Shanghai Labor Hospital, Shanghai Public Assistance Hospital, the First Hospital of the Red Cross, and the Second Hospital of the Red Cross.

The discussion then began, and the measures proposed by the Bureau of Social Affairs were accepted one by one. Finally, Chairman Tian announced that the bureau would do its best to carry out this work and hoped that it could begin on February 1st. Afterwards, refreshments were served, and the meeting adjourned.

Shipping Guild Seeks to Save Declining Industry, Attempts to Increase Freight Rates by 20%, Only Cooperative Lines Can Barely Sustain Operations 113

China's shipping industry has been severely affected by the overall economic downturn. Only the cooperative lines can barely sustain operations. The Shipping Guild is seeking to save the industry. The details are as follows:

Guild Seeks to Save Industry

Since its establishment, the Council of the China Shipping Cooperative Society originally intended to establish shipping business offices in the Yangtze River, coastal, and inland ports to handle shipping cooperation matters. However, due to the inability of state-owned and private enterprises to fully cooperate, private director Yu Qiaqing resigned in anger, leading to the suspension of council affairs and the cessation of the implementation of concrete cooperation plans. Currently, only the various shipping companies belonging to the six routes of Taipei, Shentai, Shensha, Huyong, Yangtze River, and Tongyang have independently carried out cooperation and can barely sustain operations. The remaining routes are extremely declining. The Shipping Guild has resolved to increase freight rates by 20% across the board and is currently seeking to implement this separately in an effort to save the declining shipping industry.

Cooperation on Various Lines Takes Effect

Shentai Line: Shanghai to Taizhou. The cooperators are Taizhou, Zhoushan, Chuanshan, Daxing, Pingan, and other five shipping companies, jointly leasing the Lian'an Shipping Bureau. Shentai Line: Shanghai to Pingyang. The cooperators are Ruian, Hixing, Daxing, Zhejiang, and other four shipping companies, organizing the Shenping United Bureau. Shensha Line: Shanghai to Qidong. The cooperators are Sanbei, Yuxing, Jufeng, Binji, Pingan, Dada, Daxing, Maoli, and other seven shipping companies. Tongyang Line: Shanghai to Yangzhou. The cooperators are Dada and Datong, two shipping companies. Huyong Line: Shanghai to Ningbo. The cooperators are China Merchants, Taikoo, Sanbei, and Ningshao, four shipping companies. Yangtze River Line: Shanghai to Hankou and Yichang. The cooperators are China Merchants, Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Sanbei, Ningshao, and Nissin, six shipping companies. Since the cooperation of the above six routes, they have been able to barely sustain operations during this time of decline in various industries, especially the Tongyang and Huyong lines, which are the best. This proves that the effectiveness of cooperation cannot be ignored.

Rent Reduction Committee Petitions Executive Yuan to Promptly Instruct Shanghai to Reassess Land Prices to Facilitate Rent Reduction 115

The Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee, in order to request that the central government reassess land prices in accordance with the resolutions of the Fifth National Congress in order to facilitate rent reduction, yesterday specially petitioned Premier Jiang of the Executive Yuan to promptly instruct such reassessment. The original petition stated, "Regarding the petition to promptly instruct the Shanghai authorities to reassess land prices in order to facilitate rent reduction:

Our country's economic decline has reached its extreme today. The rural economy is on the verge of bankruptcy, and urban commerce is also declining daily. The prosperous Shanghai is no longer what it once was. In addition, the January 28th Incident completely damaged its vitality. Its surface prosperity masks its actual emptiness. During this time of chaos and famine, those in power and those out of power are unable to seek revitalization in order to recover. The only fundamental relief lies in increasing income and reducing expenditure, and increasing income is best achieved through self-reliance, while reducing expenditure is most important through reducing rent. Based on this humble view, we previously presented a petition to the Fifth National Congress, which resolved to refer it to the responsible authorities for verification and handling. However, after much anticipation, no formal document has been issued.

Although the association has repeatedly appealed loudly, the result is that for every foot of progress, the forces of obstruction grow by ten feet, and the results are meager. What is the situation of real estate today, and what is its trend? Failure to reduce rent will make it impossible to seek revitalization, a fact that is already obvious in the market. Land prices exceeding actual value are a major obstacle to reducing rent. In the golden age when real estate was increasing daily, the authorities frequently assessed prices at any time. Today's real estate situation is very different from the past, but we have not yet heard of the authorities taking action to reassess land prices in accordance with reality.

Your Excellency presides over the central government and is concerned about the people's livelihood. You will not ignore this issue, which concerns the entire social livelihood. Therefore, we have described the situation below.

Please, considering the decline of Shanghai's commerce and the crisis in the social economy, promptly order the Shanghai authorities to implement a reassessment of land prices, so that rent can also be reduced accordingly. More than three million people are looking forward to it. This is respectfully submitted for your consideration. To the President of the Executive Yuan."

Ma Chijun and others, tenants of Zhongbei Gongyi Lane on Menggu Road, Zhabei, suffering from high rents due to the impact of the current situation, obtained the consent of all the tenants in the previous year and organized a Rent Reduction Branch, submitting it to the Shanghai Zhabei District Rent Reduction Committee and joining as members, starting a campaign to reduce rent and alleviate the burden on all the tenants in the lane. After repeated negotiations with the owner, Sun Lianfang, the owner, agreed to a rent reduction, charging 87.5% of the original rent based on the rent reduction amount of Nan Gongyi Lane, starting from November of last year. All the tenants in the lane are satisfied, and the rent reduction matter can be said to be concluded. It is heard that the branch has been approved for registration by the district committee, and all expenses should be borne equally by each member, with the district-issued branch seal as proof when collecting the fees.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables Request for Correction: Business Tax Bureau Sets Up Card to Intercept Ships, Essentially a Disguised Form of Old Tax, State Formulates Tax Law 118

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday cabled the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, stating, "To the esteemed Nanjing Ministry of Finance: On the 8th of this month, we received a letter from the Lacquer Industry Association stating that since the government eliminated and reformed taxes and established the Business Tax Bureau in Laohekou Town, Guanghua County, Hubei Province, several years have passed without incident. However, since the newly appointed Director Gu Shan took over, he has changed the ministry's regulations, setting up sentry posts and cards, ordering all buying houses to report and register when transporting goods down the river and inspecting documents. Furthermore, passing merchant ships must also pay taxes before being allowed to pass. All ships, both upstream and downstream, are detained, and forced to pay taxes and make up for taxes, resulting in various difficulties and exactions for merchants and inconvenience for merchants. Transactions throughout the town have been halted. After repeated consultations and discussions on relief measures by the Chamber of Commerce, the Business Tax Bureau ultimately did not take them into consideration and abolish the ship cards. Under duress, they had to write to your association for assistance. Upon approval, we checked that our firms have been sending water passengers to Laohekou Town to handle raw lacquer for many years. Now that the Business Tax Bureau has set up sentry posts and cards, it is particularly disadvantageous for the water passengers. It is appropriate to call out in unison. We specially write to your association to examine and approve, and promptly transfer it to the Ministry of Finance, ordering the Hubei Provincial Department of Finance to strictly order the Laohekou Town Business Bureau to abolish the ship cards in order to relieve merchants from their difficulties. It would be a virtuous deed. We learned that the collection of business tax is legally aimed at commercial firms, with business capital or business income as the tax base. Stores operate according to regulations, and there are accounts to check. There is no reason to set up cards along the way and check the goods. According to reports, the Laohekou Business Tax Bureau's handling is essentially a disguised form of the old tax. Although the state has formulated a business tax law, the handling of business tax by various provinces often differs from the law. The general merchants often resent that the elimination and reformation of taxes has only been a few years, and the old ways have reappeared. The associations report to the department and cable to the respected department to correct them. It is not only Hubei Province. As the saying goes, 'Block the small streams, and they will become rivers.' It seems that such malpractices are emerging daily and should be rectified early. It is appropriate to report the situation to the respected department for examination and approval, humbly requesting you to quickly inform the Hubei Department of Finance and strictly order the bureau to abolish the sentry posts and cards and stop intercepting ships and checking goods along the way in order to maintain the tax law and for the sake of fairness. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

American Tea Association Concerned about Packaging of Chinese Tea, Inspection Bureau Has Paid Close Attention 119

The Commodity Inspection Bureau previously discovered that many tea chests from tea merchants exporting tea did not have paper lining in the lead shells, resulting in lead mixing in from time to time, hindering hygiene. It had sent a letter to the Tea Industry Association to inform various tea merchants and published a notice in the newspaper. Since then, various tea merchants must line the tea with thick paper between the tea leaves and the lead shell when packing the tea in order to emphasize hygiene. The bureau recently received a letter from the American Tea Association, expressing considerable dissatisfaction with the poor packaging of Chinese exported tea and requesting that measures be taken to improve it as soon as possible. After receiving the letter, the bureau found that the packaging of tea coming to Shanghai for inspection from Anhui and Zhejiang was generally strong, but the packaging of black tea from Hubei was indeed extremely poor and easily broken. Those shipped to Europe and the United States also had the same shortcomings. It was found that this type of tea chest mostly came from Hankou and was transshipped in Shanghai. Although it is not within the scope of the bureau's inspection, since the American Tea Association has made this statement, it should pay close attention to improvement. Therefore, it sent a reply to the American Tea Association to thank them and planned to forward it to the Ministry of Industry for review and approval and send letters to the Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureau and the Municipal Tea Merchants Association for attention. The translated text of the original letter from the American Tea Association is attached below for the common viewing of tea merchants in various places. (The following is a transcription of the letter from the American Tea Association)

To the Esteemed Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau: We are writing to you as we have read the "Inspection Administration and Commerce Monthly" and are greatly impressed by your bureau's enthusiasm for the promotion of Chinese tea. However, there is one important issue that your bureau may not have considered. In order to express our assistance and cooperation, we are specially raising it for your attention. The poor packaging of your country's exported tea is undoubtedly the worst of all kinds of goods imported into the United States. This is indeed an important obstacle to the development of trade. Since the regulation that paper must be lined between the lead shell and the tea leaves, most of your packagers or tea producers have used inferior paper to stuff the shells. This inferior paper quickly breaks into pieces and mixes into the tea, which must then be removed, which is very troublesome and uneconomical. The tea chests themselves are also not strong and cannot withstand the hardships of long-distance transportation. Moreover, each chest now contains 70-75 pounds of black tea. All of these are true facts. Most merchants shipping Chinese tea to the United States are trying to reinforce the tea chests with iron hoops. Although this has a considerable effect, it cannot completely solve this difficulty. For several years, exporters have used triangular wooden strips nailed to the four corners inside the tea chests to increase support. However, based on experience, we deeply feel that this method cannot make the weak and unsecured poorly made tea chests strong. This kind of private effort to improve the packaging of Chinese tea has been going on for many years, but it has no effect. Therefore, our association has reported the above facts, hoping that your bureau can formally pay attention to them. Our association knows that your bureau's business lies in the entire Chinese industry, but tea is one of China's earliest and largest industries. Our association hopes that this letter can arouse your bureau's deepest consideration. Our association is the only representative of various tea industry groups in the United States. Our association is willing to cooperate with your bureau to correct this fundamentally important event. Your bureau may already know that the International Tea Promotion Committee has begun to promote its teas produced in Ceylon, India, Java, and Sumatra in the United States. Then, can those who care about Chinese tea be stingy with considerable expenses to eliminate this obstacle and protect their products? Respectfully submitted by the American Tea Association, December 2, 1935.

Import Tariff Rate for Wooden Boards for Pencils: Jianghai Customs Announces to Merchants 122

Jianghai Customs issued Announcement No. 1494 regarding the temporary taxation of wooden boards for pencils within the specified dimensions according to item B of No. 586 of the current import tariff, stating, "Following the order of the Ministry of Finance, it is stipulated that wooden boards for pencils, with a length of no more than 20 centimeters, a width of no more than 7.5 centimeters, and a thickness of no more than 7 centimeters, shall be temporarily classified under item B of No. 586 of the current import tariff for finished light wood, and taxed at 4.80 gold units per cubic meter, effective from January 1, 25th year. However, this method does not apply to wooden boards for pencils that exceed the specified dimensions or wooden boards that do not exceed the specified dimensions but are used for other purposes. Following this order, we should comply with it. Please inform all merchants accordingly. This is hereby announced. Tang Haian, Supervisor, and Bason, Tax Commissioner, January 9, 25th year of the Republic of China."

Mourning the Death of Ding Wenjiang, Planning to Establish a Permanent Memorial, East China Coal Mining Company Initiates, Municipal Council Sends Letter to Municipal Government Expressing Condolences 126

The death of geologist Mr. Ding Wenjiang in Hunan has brought great shock and mourning to the mining industry across the country. It is learned that the East China Coal Mining Company, in memory of Mr. Ding's lifelong dedication to academic research and his great contributions to the mining industry, has launched a joint fundraising effort with various mines across the country to establish a permanent memorial for Mr. Ding. The company has also committed 3,000 national currency dollars to initiate the effort. The original letter from the company to the Mining Association is excerpted below: "Mr. Ding Zaijun of Taixian County is the leader of the geological community in our country, with profound knowledge and extensive writings. He recently inspected coal mines in Hengyang, Hunan, and died of coal poisoning on the 6th of this month at Xiangya Hospital in Changsha. The news of his death shocked the whole country. Mr. Ding, who was not yet fifty years old, dedicated his life to geological research, enduring hardship and toil. His direct and indirect benefits to our mining industry are great and significant. In order to commemorate Mr. Ding and encourage future generations, our company requests that your association initiate a memorial method, funded by fundraising from various mines, so that Mr. Ding's spirit of dedication to academic research will be passed on permanently. Our company will commit 2,000 dollars to initiate the effort. We request that you submit this to the Council for discussion at this session so that it can be handled as soon as possible, and we look forward to your reply."

Since the death of geologist Ding Wenjiang in Hunan, all sectors at home and abroad have expressed their condolences. It is now heard that the Shanghai Public Concession's Public Works Department, because of Ding's previous tenure as the Shanghai Commercial Port Office, carefully planned Shanghai's municipal facilities and provided unwavering support for the construction of various facilities in the concession. Upon hearing of his sudden death, they were deeply saddened. The Chairman of the Board, Mr. Arnold, sent a letter to Mayor Wu, representing the Public Works Department and the citizens of the Public Concession to express condolences, stating that China had lost a scholar, statesman, and patriot in Ding's death.

Wang Xiaoliang, a Ningbo native also known as Shenghe, who works as a comprador at Hongsheng Foreign Firm at No. 40 Ningbo Road in this city, has recently, for unknown reasons, incurred the resentment of others, resulting in a villain throwing feces at him. However, the perpetrator escaped on the spot and has not yet been caught. Unexpectedly, misfortune does not come alone, and unpleasant events follow one after another. Recently, Sang Quan San, a Ningbo native residing at No. 5, Lane 217, Tongfu Road, who is engaged in military uniform business, suddenly sued Wang in the First Special District Court for fraud. Previously, Sang Quan San had a friend named Xu Zhiliang who mortgaged eight pieces of jewelry worth several tens of thousands of yuan to him, with an agreed redemption period. However, Xu was unable to redeem them on time, and Sang Quan San confiscated them according to the agreement. However, Xu Zhiliang's jewelry was originally borrowed from Xu's younger sister for mortgage. Since he was unable to redeem them, he naturally often quarreled with his brother, demanding the return of the original items. However, Xu was ultimately unable to raise the money and failed to return the pearl to its rightful owner. Around June of last year, Wang Xiaoliang, a comprador from Hongsheng Foreign Firm who was familiar with Xu's sister, suddenly visited Sang's residence. Since they were not acquainted with each other, Chen Shanrong, the manager of Xinchang Woolen Store, introduced them. Soon after, the two parties discussed the jewelry, and Wang expressed his intention to purchase it. After both parties agreed, the price was set at 21,000 yuan. Wang said that he would pay 5,000 yuan in foreign currency within one or two days, and the remaining amount would be paid in full upon delivery of the jewelry. On June 12th of last year, Sang delivered the eight pieces of jewelry to Wang at Hongsheng Foreign Firm. However, Wang suddenly said that he could not raise the full amount at the moment and could only pay 4,333 yuan first, with the remaining amount to be paid on the 14th. At that time, Sang believed that Wang Xiaoliang was a comprador and had always kept his promises, so he agreed without hesitation and did not ask for any written evidence. Who knew that from then on, Wang repeatedly postponed the agreement. At first, Sang thought that he was unable to raise the money in time, but after repeated urging, Wang denied purchasing the jewelry, saying that the jewelry was mortgaged to Sang by Xu Zhiliang. Since Xu was unable to redeem it, he had paid more than 4,300 yuan to redeem it on Xu's behalf, and that he had already returned the precious items to Xu's sister. Therefore, a dispute arose between the two parties. Although intermediaries mediated several times, it was difficult to resolve the dispute. Sang had no choice but to retain lawyer Chen Rui to file a complaint with the First Special Court, accusing Wang Xiaoliang of fraud, and attached a civil suit, demanding that he be ordered to return the eight pieces of jewelry. This case was once tried by Judge Dai Rongduo, who instructed them to wait for a rescheduled joint trial. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the continued hearing. Because the original judge Dai was on leave due to illness, the case was reassigned to Judge Yang Guanchang of the Ninth Court. After a hearing, they were again instructed to wait for a rescheduled trial.

Record of Continued Trial of Salmon Smuggling Case - Court Retrieves Customs Signature Certificate - Defendants Still Released on Original Bail for Retrial 133

In the autumn of last year, Zhu Xusheng, Zhao Lianfang, Chang Junfa, and others jointly filed a self-report with the Local Court Prosecutor's Office, accusing Xianyu merchants Zhenchang, Weng Zhaofang, Zheng Yunsheng, Zhang Benhua, Ye Zhenqin, and others of stealing salmon shipped from Soviet Russia by fraudulent means, amounting to more than 6,700 dan worth more than 70,000 yuan. Zhu Xusheng and others stated that the theft was a minor matter, but it harmed national tax revenue and was not a trivial matter. Fearing that they would be jointly suspected if the matter came to light, they had no choice but to come forward and report themselves. After the court received the report, Prosecutor Xiao Jinying investigated and verified the facts, and ordered Ye Zhenchang, Weng Zhaofang, and others to be released on bail and prosecuted under Article 339, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. Judge Wu Deying conducted several trials, but the case was not concluded due to its complexity. Details have been reported in previous newspapers. It is now known that this case was continued by Judge Wu at 3:00 PM yesterday. The plaintiffs Zhu Xusheng and others retained lawyer Zhu Ya Kui to appear in court and present their case. The defendant Ye Zhenchang retained lawyer Zhang Shizhao to appear in court and defend him. First, Ye Zhenchang testified that he was 36 years old, a native of Zhenhai, and the manager of Zhen Da Company. He denied any fraudulent activities. After the interrogator examined Ye Zhenchang's account books and the two customs signature certificates, he found a discrepancy of 134,452 pounds. The interrogator then instructed Ye Zhenchang to submit another customs signature certificate and the original certificate from the American Mellingden Public Firm (i.e., the weigher) for verification. Next, Weng Zhaofang testified that he was 53 years old, a native of Ningbo, and a street vendor at Jieshun Fish Shop on Xianyugua Street outside Xiaodongmen. Zheng Yunsheng testified that he was 41 years old, a native of Ningbo, and the manager of Shengji Fish Shop at the 16th Pier. The remaining testimonies were evasive. At this point, lawyer Zhu Ya Kui stated that the court should pay attention to the fact that the Xianyu Industry Market Price Maintenance Association was a legitimate organization. However, the defendants were very organized in their salmon smuggling and had meeting minutes that could prove it. The meeting minutes were stored at Xu Runsheng's, the manager of the Xiemao Fruit Shop at the intersection of Dongmen Road, 16th Pier. He requested that the court retrieve the minutes, which would make the inside story clearer. Recently, the defendant Ye Zhenchang and others, fearing that the situation would escalate, had begged Huang Zhensheng, the general manager of the Ice Fresh Association, to mediate with the informants Zhu Xusheng and others, with Ye and others offering 350 yuan to instruct Zhu Xusheng and others not to appear in court. At that time, Zhu Xusheng and others refused. He requested that the court order Huang Zhensheng to appear in court to clarify the truth about the mediation. The interrogator stated that the case still needed to be testified. On the one hand, he strictly instructed Ye Zhenchang to submit the customs signature certificate and the original certificate from the American Mellingden Foreign Firm at the next hearing. Ye replied that it would be difficult to submit the case and requested that an official document be issued so that he could obtain it. The interrogator did not allow it. The defendants were still released on their original bail, and then the court adjourned.

Rickshaw Pullers in Special District - Part of Them on Strike Yesterday - Arrested Rickshaw Pullers Ordered by Court to Be Released on Bail Pending Trial - Association Submits Petitions to Taxpayers for Assistance 136

Following the conflict between rickshaw pullers in the Special District and the Mutual Aid Association, a portion of the rickshaw pullers announced a strike yesterday. 19 of the arrested rickshaw pullers were released, and the remaining 23 were handed over to the court on bail, with sentencing scheduled for Monday. Six rickshaw pullers were arrested in the two concessions for deflating tires. Vehicle damage occurred in Zhabei. The Rickshaw Pullers Association petitioned local rotation associations for assistance. The situation is reported as follows:

Arrested Rickshaw Pullers - 19 Released

Of the rickshaw pullers arrested in the Jiading Road incident with the Mutual Aid Association, a total of 42 people were arrested. Yesterday morning, the head of the Jiading Road Police Station questioned the truth separately. As a result, 19 people, including Shu Huajin, Xue Yuquan, Xing Hongyi, Luan Zhenzhao, Yin Yongshan, and Zhu Richang, were found to be unrelated to the case and were released immediately. The remaining 23 people, including Cang Gongsen, Zhu Dekun, Luo Deguang, Ma Taizhi, Dai Zhugui, Ji Decai, Li Youfu, Zhu Xitong, Cheng Shuangquan, Wang Guangtian, Han Ruben, Ji Songgao, Sun Yicai, Wang Yuehong, Han Rugen, Chen Hengkuan, Yu Zhijiang, Yin Yonggui, Chi Haishan, Huang Amao, Xu Fuchang, Xing Riqing, and Bao Degao, were all detained.

23 People Sent to Court

They were sent to the First Special District Local Court yesterday morning, where Judge Jiang Shuzi conducted the trial. First, the police lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated the circumstances of the incident, requesting an investigation of the defendants for violating Article 150 of the Criminal Law for disrupting order and Article 354 for property damage. Next, the Western head of the Jiading Road Police Station reported the results of the investigation. The officials of the Mutual Aid Association, with the exception of Zhang Dengying, who was still in the hospital, Deputy Secretary-General Chen Chunbao, Hu Kangning, a teacher at the association's affiliated elementary school, Gu Bufan, Zhou Pengnian, and the doorman No. 1327, all successively arrived in court to identify the perpetrators among the defendants and presented the photos taken after the destruction of the items and the slips of paper found on the walls of the association with the rickshaw pullers' request for loans to get through the New Year. Judge Jiang then interrogated each of the defendants one by one, and the defendants' statements generally said that they went to the association to request the announcement of the accounts for 17 months and to borrow the auditorium to hold a memorial service for Yang Binshan, who was beaten to death by rickshaw owners, and all denied destroying property or assaulting people. They retained two lawyers, Zhu Shuzhen and Xi Shichang, to defend them, arguing that four of the defendants were also injured in the assault and requested that a forensic doctor be allowed to examine them. Judge Jiang stated that it was noon and ordered each of the defendants to pay 50 yuan bail and rescheduled the trial. As for the defendants' lawyers' request to examine the injuries, he orally instructed the defendants to obtain bail and then legally submit for examination on their own.

Fear of Defendant's Destruction - Vehicles Greatly Reduced

At 10:00 PM the night before, in the Zhabei area, more than 40 unemployed rickshaw pullers blocked vehicles in a cold and quiet place and had a dispute with the rickshaw pullers on duty. As a result, more than 30 vehicles were damaged. The rickshaw owners, contractors, and rickshaw pullers were all worried about the incident. Therefore, only 50% of the vehicles were released in Zhabei yesterday morning, 20% in Nanshi, and 80-90% in Husi, Hozhong, and Hodong. It is estimated that about 3,000 vehicles were suspended from operation, while the remaining 7,000 vehicles were operating as usual. However, many unemployed rickshaw pullers continued to go out and deflate tires.

Authorities Protect - Suspension of Petitions

More than 10,000 rickshaw pullers were on strike yesterday morning, and together with more than 2,000 unemployed rickshaw pullers, they were all causing trouble. The police authorities of the Chinese Concession have strictly ordered their subordinates to protect the operation of rickshaws along the way to maintain local peace and tranquility, and to arrest those who destroy them at any time. The Rickshaw Pullers Association originally planned to petition the party and government organs yesterday morning, but because the arrested rickshaw pullers had to be sent to the court and needed to be present to observe the proceedings, it was temporarily suspended.

Taxpayers, etc. - Agree to Provide Assistance

The Special District Rickshaw Pullers Association sent representatives Cang Gongwen and Zhou Weigao at 2:00 PM yesterday, preparing documents to petition Zhong Si, the local affairs manager of the Ministry of Public Works, and He Dekui, the co-manager, reporting on the process. Zhong and He agreed to thoroughly investigate and handle the matter in accordance with the law. They then went to the Taxpayers' Chinese Association, where Tao Leqin met them and agreed to provide legal assistance. They then went to the First Special District Citizens' Federation, where Liu Zhongying met them and agreed to negotiate. The representatives then supplemented the petition to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and scheduled to petition the Municipal Government and others this morning.

Ms. Chen Speaks On: Gender Equality in Soviet Russia Allows Women to Attain Men's Status 137

A mainland newspaper reports: Miss Chen, daughter of former Foreign Minister Chen Youren, who resided in Soviet Russia for many years, is soon to travel to Russia to participate in the Moscow International Dance Conference. On Thursday, she delivered a speech at the International Art Theater in this city about the status of women in Soviet Russia. She stated that there are certain absolute truths that must be understood: The economic structure of Soviet Russia is completely different from that of capitalist countries, and therefore the social system that arises from it is also completely different from those of other countries. In Soviet Russia, women have absolute equality of opportunity with men. There is complete equality between the sexes in all respects. In fields such as science, the Red Army, aviation factories, and various other industries, there are many women occupying important positions. If a woman's talent surpasses that of a man, she can attain the man's position. Salaries are determined based on talent. If a woman's work ability exceeds that of a man, her salary will be higher than the man's, without any difference due to her gender. Marriage in Soviet Russia is very simple. Marriage never involves financial matters. Even students can get married, because their expenses are provided by the government during their studies. Divorce is now more difficult than before. Each divorce case requires a fee of ten rubles. If there are children, they are always raised by the mother, and the father must pay one-third of the children's maintenance expenses. There is no alimony system in Soviet Russia. Soviet women do not need to be skilled in household management. The Western view of women's position in the family is scorned by Soviet Russia. The aim of Soviet Russia is to free women from the shackles of household drudgery and enable them to engage in more beneficial social work. Pregnant women are entitled to two months of rest before and after childbirth, while receiving full pay. In addition, the state provides a monthly allowance of fifty rubles for a certain period, followed by twenty rubles for a certain period. Pregnant women receive good care from doctors without charge. Therefore, Soviet women are not afraid of pregnancy. Contraceptive methods can be inquired about from doctors. If one wants to have an abortion, it must be discussed with a committee, explaining the reasons for wanting to do so. If the reasons are sufficient, it can be carried out; otherwise, it cannot be done without permission. There are no brothels or prostitutes in Soviet Russia. Former prostitutes have been sent to correctional institutions to be taught how to become good citizens. Criminals are also treated this way, without discrimination, and are not dismissed as uncivilized.

Assaulting a Tram Conductor: Perpetrators Sentenced to One Year Imprisonment, Chen Huaxiang and Chen Genbao Detained for One Year Each, Liu Zhen Given a Three-Year Suspended Sentence and Initially Allowed Bail 138

Chen Huaxiang, a 24-year-old local resident, lives at No. 41 Luban Road, Huajie, and works as an auto coppersmith. Chen Genbao is the same age as Huaxiang, lives in a bungalow without a number in the Lu Family Lane, Xujiahui Road, French Concession, and works as a painter. On December 21st of last year, at 7 p.m., the two men boarded tram No. 40 on route 6 of the French Tramway Company from Xiaobeimen, French Concession, heading towards Xieqiao. They refused to purchase tickets. Mu Xiaoshan (32 years old, from Nanjing), the No. 218 conductor on the tram, reprimanded them and insisted they buy tickets, leading to a verbal altercation. The Chens harbored resentment. After getting off the tram at Xieqiao, they gathered accomplices and thugs to wait at the intersection of Xujiahui Road and Beile Road. When the tram returned from Lujiawan and arrived at Beile Road, Mu Xiaoshan, the conductor, got off to switch the red and green lights. The two Chens immediately led the thugs to swarm over, dragging Mu into Huajie and beating him severely, with fists and feet. They also stabbed him in the head, face, lower abdomen, and other places with knives. Mu cried out loudly for help. No. 87 of the French police heard the commotion and rushed to intervene, but Chen and his gang threatened and stopped them with handguns, preventing them from approaching. The police officer then called the Lujiawan Central Police Station, and a large number of detectives rushed to the scene. The perpetrators had already scattered and fled. Only the injured Mu Xiaoshan was lying on the ground, moaning incessantly. Mu was taken to Guangci Hospital for treatment. The police then initiated negotiations, and by 4 p.m. the next day, the French police arrested the two Chens, took them back to the police station, and sent them to the Special No. 2 Court for interrogation and detention. The investigation was postponed for further questioning. Details of the situation were published in this newspaper on December 25th of last year. Later, another accomplice, Liu Zhen (who runs a bicycle shop in Gaochang Temple), was apprehended and brought to the court to be investigated in conjunction with the case. The court also appointed a forensic doctor to go to Guangci Hospital to examine the victim's injuries. The French Police Department filed a public prosecution against the defendants on charges of assault. After careful investigation by Judge Wang Wangxu, head of the Criminal Court, at 10 a.m. yesterday, Judge Wang went to Criminal Division One to order the defendants to be brought before the court for sentencing. Chen Huaxiang, Chen Genbao, and Liu Zhen were each sentenced to one year of imprisonment for jointly injuring a person's body. Liu Zhen was given a three-year suspended sentence. During the appeal period, his father was responsible for bailing him out. The two Chens were returned to the detention center.

Shanghai Municipal Council Legal Department: Work Report for December 142

According to the Legal Department's report for December, the Council filed a total of 7,447 lawsuits in the First Special District Court and the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court this month. This includes 6,203 administrative cases and 1,414 criminal cases. In the administrative cases, 4,570 defendants failed to appear for trial, and the bail they had paid was immediately confiscated. A total of 1,615 administrative cases were completed, with 1,611 found guilty and 4 acquitted. In the criminal cases, 13 were withdrawn due to insufficient evidence. A total of 1,214 cases were completed, with 1,071 found guilty and 143 acquitted. In total, 2,829 administrative and criminal cases were completed this month, with 2,682 found guilty and 147 acquitted. In addition, there were 170 criminal self-prosecution cases and 280 cases filed by the Works and Health Departments for violations. The Vehicle Department filed 994 lawsuits. This month, the conviction rate was 99.8% for administrative cases and 88.2% for criminal cases, for a total conviction rate of 94%. Regarding appeals, the Council filed 7 cases with the Higher Court. There were 13 appeal cases filed by the Council that had not yet been concluded by the end of December: one with the Supreme Court and 12 with the Higher Court. The defendants filed a total of 67 appeal cases, including 9 with the Supreme Court and 58 with the Higher Court. 56 appeal cases filed by the defendants were concluded, with 45 appeals rejected, one withdrawn, one original sentence increased, 8 original sentences reduced, and one defendant acquitted. There were 129 appeal cases filed by the defendants that had not yet been concluded by the end of the month, including 59 with the Supreme Court and 70 with the Higher Court. Furthermore, there were 14 requests from outside the Settlement for the transfer of suspects, involving 28 suspects. All were approved for transfer due to sufficient prima facie evidence.

Prisoner Ward to Be Built in Guangci Hospital 143

The Shanghai French Concession Police Department has traditionally sent sick prisoners from the Concession to Guangci Hospital on Kimpather Road for treatment. There was no separate prisoner ward. Upon the request of the French Municipal Council, the French Concession Charity Association took on the task of building a prisoner ward in Guangci Hospital last year, with the Association subsidizing construction costs of 7,000 French francs. The ward has now been completed. The Association has sent a letter to the French Municipal Council thanking them for their enthusiasm for public welfare.

Traveler Commits Suicide by Poison Due to Hopeless Situation 144

Due to unemployment and economic pressure, a traveler named Hu Ri, 31 years old from Guangdong, checked into the Juxingxin Inn at No. 434, North Zhejiang Road (North of Hua'anfang), Zhabei, the night before. He paid two jiao for a bed. The inn's regulations stipulate that guests staying in the bed-only section are not allowed to linger in the inn during the day. Therefore, at 10 a.m., any guest who has not gotten up must be urged to do so. Tea server Cao Bingsheng went to the bed at the designated time and saw that the traveler surnamed Hu had not gotten up. He called out several times but received no response. He opened the curtain and was shocked to see Hu's face was pale. Knowing he had taken poison, he immediately reported to the innkeeper Cao Zhupei, who reported to the Tianbaoli Sub-Station of the Menggu Road Police Station. Officer Pan immediately instructed the innkeeper to send the traveler to Pushan Hospital on Xinmin Road. However, too much time had passed, and he died before treatment could be administered. A bottle of liquid was found on the deceased's bed. It was a four-ounce bottle of Lysol. It is believed that this was taken, making it impossible to save him. The deceased had over ten pawn tickets and a note written in pencil on his person. It generally stated that because he was unemployed, suffering from economic pressure, and had repeatedly borrowed money from relatives and friends, he had run out of options and had resorted to this extreme measure. The body is currently at the hospital. The deceased had a shaved head and was wearing a black cotton-padded jacket with a velvet lining and striped white velvet pants with yellow and black socks. The local bailiff will report to the Shanghai Local Court today to request an autopsy.

Further News on the Drug Case Uncovered at the South Railway Station 146

On November 23rd of last year, a large quantity of drugs, weighing over a hundred pounds and disguised as the medicinal herb "Yu Zhu," was discovered at the South Railway Station. It was packed in six burlap sacks and transported by Wang Changgen to the South Railway Station, where it was entrusted to the Daxing Transportation Company for transport to Zhejiang. At that time, the Daxing Company's representative at the station asked Wang Changgen for an invoice and a letter from the consignee. Because the language was unclear, the company sent someone to accompany him to retrieve them. Wang Changgen attempted to escape midway, but the accompanying person called for the police and he was apprehended. Sensing something was amiss, they took him to the Second District Bureau. The bureau sent Shen Wenda to the station to inspect the goods. Upon opening the sacks, they discovered small packages inside the Yu Zhu, which, upon inspection, turned out to be raw drug materials. While Shen Wenda was supervising the inspection, he noticed a man loitering nearby who looked suspicious. The police detained him. Wang Changgen then identified Hu Shimo as the mastermind behind the transportation. The police took him to the bureau for questioning. He confessed that the ultimate boss was Ye Zicai, who was also arrested and brought to justice. Various Shanghai newspapers have reported on this. However, there are conflicting accounts of the truth of the matter. Some say that only three packs of drug materials were found in the entire shipment, mixed with over a hundred pounds of Taikoo sugar. Based on current drug prices, the total value is no more than three hundred yuan. Calling it a large quantity refers to the combined weight of the Taikoo sugar. Others say that since Hu Shimo saw Wang Changgen being escorted by the police to open the sacks at the station, why didn't he escape? It shows the retribution for trafficking in drugs and harming people. Others say that Ye Zicai's family fortune is less than modest, so where did he get the large sum of money to purchase and traffic in drugs? It is puzzling.

Letter Requesting Temporary Suspension of Photography Requirement for Domestic Servants: Sixth Division of the Second Special District Citizens' Association Writes to the French Inspector General 155

The French Concession Police Department stipulates that all domestic servants must have three photos taken: one to be submitted to the police station, one to be submitted to the employer, and one to be kept by the domestic servant placement agency, i.e., the "broker's shop," to prevent abuses. All "broker's shops" within the concession were notified to implement this requirement. This caused many domestic servants to flock to placement agencies in the Public Concession to seek employment. Employers also went to placement agencies in the Public Concession to hire domestic servants. The police department was unable to interfere. This led to a sharp decline in the business of placement agencies in the French Concession. Yesterday, more than ten agencies, including Jinguiji, Wang Lao Broker, Hong Lao Broker, Hongji Li Piao Broker, Yifeilin Zhe Broker, Shanghai Domestic Servant Placement Agency, and Liu Lao Broker on Julida Road, jointly wrote to the Sixth Division of the Second Special District Citizens' Association for assistance. The Association then wrote to Faber, the French Inspector General of the French Concession Police Department, requesting a temporary suspension of the requirement. The original letter stated: "We have received a joint letter from more than ten member placement agencies, including Jinguiji. They state that the French authorities recently stipulated that all domestic servants introduced must have three photos taken: one to be deposited with the police station, one to be deposited with the employer, and one to be kept by the placement agency. However, the Public Concession has no such regulation. This has caused many domestic servants to regard the French Concession with fear and flock to the Public Concession. This has caused the members' businesses to be unusually slow, but the monthly rent and taxes cannot be reduced. Therefore, we request that you transfer to the French Inspector General that the photography requirement is difficult to implement and request that it be rescinded. Even if the French authorities must implement it, please suspend it temporarily and wait until the Public Concession has the same regulations before implementing it at the same time. This will avoid domestic servants seeking employment in the Public Concession and employers hiring domestic servants from placement agencies in the Public Concession. This will ensure uniformity and maintain business." Based on this, the claims made by Jinguiji and others are indeed true. Currently, most domestic servants are seeking employment at domestic servant placement agencies in the Public Concession, and most employers are hiring domestic servants from placement agencies in the Public Concession. Therefore, we are writing to the Inspector General to request a temporary suspension of the photography requirement. If it must be implemented, then please wait until the authorities in the Public Concession have the same regulations before proceeding at the same time, in order to maintain the business of the domestic servant placement agencies in the French Concession. We deeply appreciate your understanding and hope to hear from you. Sincerely, To Mr. Faber, French Inspector General, French Concession.

Correspondence 163

To the esteemed Editor: In the special issue of your newspaper yesterday on the Da Sun Company, a section of my conversation contains discrepancies with the facts. I joined Fu Ji Construction Company in 1932 (Republican Year 21). At that time, the Guangzhou Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall had already been completed, and the people in charge were Huang Ziqiang, Zhou Jingxi, Zhou Shuzhi, and Pan Zhihao. The Nanjing Cemetery of Martyred Soldiers began construction in February 1931 (Republican Year 20), and the people in charge were Qiu Xianming, Zhou Jingxi, and Weng Cunlin. The projects I have managed include the 22-story building of the Four Banks Joint Savings Society and the Da Sun Company. Moreover, the company does not have the title of "Chief Engineer of the Entire Company." All important plans, etc., are the responsibility of Mr. Tao Guilin, the owner and general manager of the company. I am sending this letter specifically to clarify this and hope that you will make the correction. Respectfully, Jin Fulin, Fu Ji Construction Company, January 10.

To the esteemed Editor: I am writing on behalf of my client, Mr. Zhang Guanlin, who claims that he read in the "Local News" column of your newspaper on January 10th an article entitled "Son Makes Things Difficult for Old Father, Father Commits Suicide in Anger." After reading the article, he was extremely shocked. After investigation, the reported details are completely unfounded and far from the truth. Guanlin is the eldest son of Zhang Ronghua and his second wife, Yu, and he is a law-abiding businessman who does not involve himself in external affairs. Furthermore, he has no disagreements with his father at all. This sudden death is completely unexpected. The stepmother, Zhou, did not inform Guanlin to attend the funeral and fulfill his filial duties according to etiquette. The inside story is clearly suspicious. Moreover, the original report stated that Guanlin had bullied him to death, that he was born to an outside woman, and that he was adopted into the family of Cha Jiren as a son-in-law. These claims are all baseless rumors and are extremely damaging to Guanlin's reputation and credibility. Therefore, he has commissioned this lawyer to write to your newspaper to request a correction. Accordingly, I am writing this letter on his behalf and requesting that you investigate and make a correction to avoid further disputes and maintain our friendly relations. Respectfully, Chen Xuelu, Lawyer, January 10.

Shanghai Office of the Academic Work Advisory Center Issues a Notice: Applications for Registration Must Be Completed Accurately and in Detail 172

The Shanghai Office of the National Academic Work Advisory Center received Notice No. 10 from the Nanjing Academic Work Advisory Center yesterday. The notice stated that the center handles the registration and job placement of graduates from domestic and foreign colleges and universities. The registration procedures have been simplified, and the placement is carefully considered. The original intention was to ensure that talented people could be put to use and that the unemployed could find jobs. However, it has been found that recently, there have been cases of inaccurate and inconsistent information in the registration and submitted resumes. Applicants have exaggerated their qualifications and attempted to deceive the center. It should be known that there is no greater form of self-deception. The center adheres to the principle of selecting people based on their abilities. Those who submit resumes containing false information will not be recommended for job placement. It is hereby notified that in the future, when applying for registration and requesting job placement, applicants must accurately and in detail fill in their academic qualifications and work experience, and must not be frivolous or excessive, in order to facilitate job placement and avoid self-destruction. The Shanghai Office has posted the original notice. In the future, all personnel who apply for registration and request job placement from the Shanghai Office must accurately and in detail fill in their applications. Those who attempt to deceive the office will not be recommended for job placement.
