A Retrospective and Prospect of Educational Administration (Part 1) - 5:30 PM, January 9, Lecture at the Central Broadcasting Station 174

— Lei Zhen

Today is the first time in the 25th year of the Republic of China that I have come to the broadcasting station to give a speech. At the beginning of this new year, we should naturally look back on the work of the past year, and based on past experience, make plans for the future. In the past year, the Ministry of Education's facilities for educational administration cannot be described in detail in this short period of time. Now, I will give a brief report on the more important new facilities:

(1) Reorganizing Schools Above the Specialized Level

In recent years, the Ministry of Education has spared no effort in reorganizing higher education. The reasons and methods for the reorganization are not based on subjective opinions, but entirely on objective facts. Before the reorganization, a large number of inspectors were dispatched annually to various places to inspect schools above the specialized level. The inspectors were all experts, and the inspection method was to adopt a departmental inspection system. In the 23rd year, more than 40 schools were inspected. The results of the inspections have been ordered to improve. In the spring of the 24th year, more staff were dispatched to various places to inspect the actual situation of the schools' improvement in the past year. More than 90 schools were inspected. Looking at the inspection reports, the schools have made considerable improvements on the Ministry's instructions on various key points for improvement, such as reorganizing departments, enriching equipment, cracking down on absenteeism, strict enrollment, focusing on moral education and research, and strictly implementing the system of full-time teachers and staff. However, a few schools, limited by the environment, have shown little achievement. The Ministry of Education has re-instructed and ordered them to comply. The reorganization of departments is based on two principles: one is the merger of duplicate or excessive departments, and the other is the reorganization of departments that lack teachers and equipment and have no hope of development. The former are mostly liberal arts departments, and the latter are mostly practical science departments. In recent years, the reorganization of university departments has gradually become rationalized, unlike the chaotic situation of a few years ago.

(2) Emphasizing Practical Science

In order to prevent the abnormal development of liberal arts and practical science, and to remedy the drawbacks of talent surplus and shortage, the Ministry of Education has specially stipulated the enrollment ratio of various departments in universities to correct the excessive development of liberal arts and gradually increase the number of practical science talents to meet the needs of national construction. In recent years, the number of practical science students has gradually increased compared with the previous few years, and at the same time, the number of liberal arts freshmen has also gradually decreased. Although the amount of increase and decrease is not very large at present, there is indeed a trend of increase and decrease. At the same time, the increase of practical science departments is also actively underway. If manpower and financial resources are limited and cannot be expanded in fact, then orders are given to establish lectureships in order to instill practical science. In recent years, the increase of practical science has included six colleges, three departments, two subjects, and six lectureships. The subsidies for private schools above the specialized level also pay considerable attention to the enrichment of practical science.

(3) Implementing the Degree Granting Law

The formulation of the Degree Granting Law is entirely to improve academic standards. It has now been resolved by the Legislative Yuan and presented to the National Government for promulgation. The most important point is that the degree adopts a three-level system of bachelor's, master's, and doctoral degrees. The travel date is also planned by the Ministry of Education and presented to the National Government for promulgation, which has been implemented since July 1935, and the Ministry has ordered all universities, colleges, and educational halls and bureaus to be informed. The detailed rules for degree classification and the detailed rules for the master's degree examination have also been formulated and promulgated by the Ministry of Education.

(4) Holding Qualification Examinations for Students of Unregistered and Closed Private Schools Above the Specialized Level

This examination has been held several times in the past. The Ministry of Education has examined the results, classified them by grade, and issued transfer certificates. However, there are still many students in unregistered private schools who are waiting and unwilling to move forward, losing their opportunities. Afterwards, they have repeatedly requested relief. In the winter of the 24th year, another examination was held in Beijing and Shanghai. It was ordered that public and registered private schools above the specialized level must not accept transfer students from unregistered and closed private schools above the specialized level, as well as students from unregistered and closed senior secondary schools, from the 24th year onwards, in order to show restrictions. The examination has now been completed. A total of more than 180 students in Beijing and more than 1,500 students in Shanghai participated in the examination. The test papers are being graded and will be announced soon.

(5) Implementing Compulsory Education

The implementation of compulsory education has been planned by the Ministry of Education for many years. This time, in accordance with the resolution of the Fifth Plenary Session of the Fourth National Congress, the outline of the provisional measures for the implementation of compulsory education and the detailed rules for implementation were formulated and promulgated by the Executive Yuan in May of last year. The implementation content is divided into three phases: the first phase is from August 1935 to July 1940, running one-year short-term primary schools; the second phase is from August 1940 to July 1944, running two-year short-term primary schools; the third phase is from August 1944, the compulsory education period is four years. In addition to running short-term primary schools, it also implements the promotion of junior primary schools, enriches the number of original classes, strictly implements the two-part system, improves private schools, and pilots itinerant education. During the period of compulsory education, short-term primary schools do not charge tuition fees, and student textbooks are also provided free of charge by the schools. Healthy school-age children in various places are supervised by local educational administrative agencies to force their parents to enroll. In terms of funding, it is borne and raised by the local government, and the central government provides appropriate subsidies. This year, the central government's subsidy for compulsory education in various places is 2.4 million yuan, plus border education funds and Gengzi compensation funds, for a total of 3.2 million yuan. The first phase of compulsory education has now begun, and the provinces and cities have reported the situation to the Ministry, which is very smooth.

(6) Implementing Children's Year

The Ministry of Education aims to awaken the national masses, pay attention to children's education, protect children's physical and mental health, and seek children's welfare, so as to complete children's physical, mental, and social abilities. Therefore, there is the implementation of Children's Year. The implementation period is from August 1, 1935, to July 31 of this year. The central government is composed of the Ministry of Education, the Ministry of Interior, and the Ministry of Industry, together with the China Children's Welfare Association, to organize the National Children's Year Implementation Committee. The provinces, cities, and counties are composed of educational administrative and health administrative agencies, as well as children's career groups, to organize the Children's Year Implementation Committees of the provinces, cities, and counties. There are 25 provinces and cities that have been established and reported to the General Association. Regarding the work plan, the outline of the implementation measures and the implementation procedures are formulated. The important work is roughly divided into four categories: children's education, children's health, children's protection, and the organization of children's happiness groups. They are carried out separately according to the implementation procedures. In this year, there are four important children's exhibitions: The National Children's Book Exhibition will be held in Beijing for about a week on January 31; The National Children's Toys and Teaching Aids Exhibition will be held in Beijing in April; The National Children's Health Exhibition will be held in Beijing in May; The National Children's Painting Exhibition will be held in Shanghai, date to be determined (undetermined).

Miscellaneous News from the Aryans 181

High-Speed Motion Picture Camera for Finish Line Records

For all speed finish line records at this Berlin convention, it has been decided to adopt a state-of-the-art high-speed camera as the standard for judging. This camera also comes equipped with timing components, both of which can be activated simultaneously during recording. It is adjusted using a special device based on the alternating current frequency, offering six speed levels with the fastest at one-thousandth of a second, followed by one-hundredth of a second, one-tenth, and so on, ensuring no wasted time in recording.

This device is a small, variable machine that can operate continuously, capturing between a hundred to sixteen photographs per second. Matters like determining race rankings, which were previously difficult to observe in detail at slow-motion speeds, can now be distinctly judged. This camera underwent various trials at last year's European Athletics Championships, yielding very positive results. As such, judging errors in the sports world can be entirely eliminated from now on.

Convention Car Advertising

Since last fall, the advertising train planned by the 11th Aryan Olympics Advertising Committee has appeared in various German cities and neighborhoods, conducting domestic public advertising. This train consists of two freight cars, each equipped with four-wheeled trucks, with a large curtain stretched between the two cars. Visitors can freely enter and exit, finding within them various models and films related to sports, as well as historical items about the Aryans, allowing the public along the route to immediately grasp the historical significance of the Aryan Olympics. This train does not stay long in any location, with the entire route planned to cover over ten thousand miles or seven thousand miles, starting from major cities.

The Aryan Olympics Giant Bell, Symbol of Peace

This bell, cast by the Bocbhum Steel Forging Company on August 14th of last year, weighs seventeen tons. The casting requires several weeks for cooling. It is now complete and will be transported to the top of the memorial tower at the convention site, to be permanently hung. The tower is approximately two hundred and sixty feet high, and from August 1st of this year, the massive bronze mouth will resonate deeply in our ears.

During the 1855 World Exposition held in Paris, three giant bells manufactured by the same company were displayed, selected from a large number of bells made of "cast steel plates," worth more than double today. Since then, the company has manufactured and exported over one hundred thousand giant bells to countries around the world, including industrially developed nations like England, France, America, and Italy, further demonstrating their superior sound quality as the best in the world. As a friendly nation, we are participating in the grand event. The resonance of the Aryan Olympics on August 1st, combined with the simultaneous ringing of giant bells from around the world, creates a harmonious sound akin to that of brothers, making the symbol of peace all the more joyful.

The True Winner

The Chairman of the Aryan Olympics Committee of the South American Argentine Republic broadcast a radio speech on the true spirit of winning in the Aryan Olympics, the gist of which is as follows:

A winner must be persevering, capable of enduring hardship, full of fighting spirit, and also possess self-reasoning, correct mistakes, blame failures on their own faults, and discover and heal their weaknesses. If one desires greatness, then one must work hard to improve oneself, take the strengths of others to make up for one's own shortcomings.

Furthermore, a winner should repeatedly practice each task ten or even a hundred times to achieve its effect, and be prepared to give up temporary happiness such as walks, pleasure, fame, and contemplation to strengthen their character and fulfill the primary conditions, so that victory will naturally be solid.

The so-called winner is one who pursues an ideal undertaking, but instead of resting in a dream realm, should work hard in that dream realm to make it a reality.

Children's Education Novel

Little Men (1)(4)(8) 186

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Most of the boys coldly ignored him, but Dan, though he said he hated him because he had no courage, protected him fiercely, and would immediately punish anyone who dared to insult him or frighten him with his old fists. His loyalty to his friends was not inferior to that of Xiao Mei, but the refinement of the way he expressed it was different.

One afternoon, Dan was sitting by the creek, intently studying the various habits of a small spider's home, when he suddenly heard a short conversation over there. It turned out that Nada had recently felt like he had thorns in his back, and wanted to be sure who the real culprit was; because one or two boys had begun to suspect that they might be wrong, Naide continued to deny it, and humbled himself to accept people's neglect. This suspicion made Nada unable to bear it any longer. He privately disobeyed Mr. Pei's clear admonition and questioned Naide several times. This time, seeing Naide reading a book alone in the shade of the wall, he could not help but stop and try again on that taboo topic. Before Dan arrived, he had been interrogating Naide for ten minutes. The first few words that the spider scholar heard were Naide saying in a patient and pleading tone:

"Don't do this, Nada! Ah, don't do this! I can't tell you, because I don't know. You shouldn't bother me privately. Uncle Pei told you not to make things difficult for me. If Dan was here, you wouldn't dare do this."

"Bah! Am I afraid of Dan?" He's just a bad sack. I think the money of Taomo was not taken by others, but by him. You know it, but you just don't want to say it. Say it now!"

One Year of Foreign Exchange (Continued) 189

— Ci

In the past three or four years, our country has been hovering under this kind of policy of the great powers, becoming the object of their dumping policies, the tail-end of their surplus commodities. The main countries that have a close economic relationship with our country, such as Britain, Japan, and the United States, have all seen their currencies depreciate by between 40% and 60%. The United States' increase in the price of silver is a further step to increase the purchasing power of our country's currency, but it has put our country in an extremely difficult situation for the past two years.

If we want to analyze the meaning represented by the numbers in the table above, we can see that in 1929 (the 18th year of the Republic of China), the countries had not yet abandoned the gold standard, and the price of silver had not fallen, so our country's foreign exchange remained normal. In 1930, the price of silver began to fall sharply, and our country's foreign exchange also fell with it. In the 18th year, the British exchange rate was 20.524 pence, but in the 19th year it fell to 14.769 pence (as did the American and Japanese exchange rates). It reached its extreme in the 20th year, with the British exchange rate only being a little over 12 pence, the American exchange rate at 22.2 yuan, and the Japanese exchange rate at 45.2 yuan, the lowest prices seen in more than ten years. (To be continued)

Securities. Reaction After Frequent Falls in Public Bonds. Market Sentiment Rebounds at Closing. Market Prices Rise Slowly. 190

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange did not show a strong market situation. Although there was a sign of recovery after a period of fatigue in the afternoon market, it was only due to gold speculators covering their short positions and retail investors buying in following the trend. No. 4 initially lay dormant, taking the opportunity to raise prices when they rose. The low-pressure atmosphere in the market has not subsided. Large investors continued to sell, with Nos. 48, 54, and 78 consistently selling. Rumors circulated about reducing interest rates on bonds, or extending the principal repayment period, or issuing new bonds to recall old bonds to achieve unification. According to investigations, these rumors had some basis. Therefore, the current focus of market price fluctuations is whether there will be any changes to these bonds, and whether the situation in Suiyuan will expand, both of which are sufficient to influence the market situation. Women's Special Edition

My Views on Women's Issues 201

— Liu Yazi

Since being elected as a Central Supervisory Committee Member of the Fourth National Congress of the Kuomintang, I have rarely spoken. According to the Party's discipline, members should not freely express opinions externally, especially since I am only a nominal committee member. However, this time, due to the special circumstances and the request of brothers Shoujuan and Jiping to write for the Shenbao Women's Special Edition, I have to make an exception.

First, I must state that I advocate the theory of evolution in everything. However, my theory of evolution is not entirely imported but includes native Chinese elements. I don't understand classical studies, nor do I greatly admire Confucius, but I strongly agree with the theories of the Great Harmony in the Book of Rites and the Three Ages of Gongyang. Naturally, regardless of whether it is truly a doctrine of Confucius or a fabrication by scholars of the Han Dynasty. I have not deeply studied Sun Yat-sen's Three Principles of the People, but I believe that nationalism, democracy, and the people's livelihood should be divided into three stages. Thus, integrating the past and present, and combining the old and new, we can say that Gongyang's Age of Disorder corresponds to Sun Yat-sen's stage of nationalism, which is also what modern Western scholars call the stage of feudal society. Gongyang's Age of Ascending Peace, the Age of Moderate Prosperity in the Book of Rites, corresponds to Sun Yat-sen's stage of democracy, which is also what Western scholars call the stage of capitalist society. Gongyang's Age of Great Peace, the Age of Great Harmony in the Book of Rites, corresponds to Sun Yat-sen's stage of the people's livelihood, which is also what Western scholars call the stage of socialist society. The above is the backbone of my advocated theory of evolution.

Applying this to women's issues, the idea that women should not speak outside the home, should not hear opinions from outside, and should follow their husbands no matter who they are, is, of course, a feature of feudal society. Organizing small families, participating in productive enterprises, and breaking away from feudal shackles, yet living under the money system, selling labor power insufficiently, followed by selling sexual organs, is unavoidable in capitalist society. Later, the ideal of everyone contributing according to their ability and receiving according to their needs, breaking down the marriage system, and advocating free love can only be achieved in a socialist society. Sun Yat-sen urged us to catch up head-on, of course, to overthrow the system of feudal society, but not to be satisfied with simply following capitalism. Everything is like this, and women's issues are no exception.

Speaking of this, I want to look at the actual situation of the current world. Hitler wants women to return to the kitchen, which is a concern about the phenomenon of capitalist decline. He simply wants to reverse the car back to the old home of feudal society, but how can this road lead anywhere? In our country, there is an even more deformed situation: on the one hand, rural women are still living the hellish life of the 18th century; on the other hand, urban women have already embarked on the path of capitalist decline. The surge in imported cosmetics and the willingness of women to regard themselves as playthings and commodities are not their sins, but merely symptoms of the end of the century, which have already festered beyond repair. When men are in extreme distress, they use alcohol and women to escape. Why can't women adopt the same attitude? Therefore, advocating new female virtues and new principles of being a virtuous wife and good mother, though well-intentioned, is probably still the wrong medicine.

To solve women's issues, we must solve the entire social system. Gongyang's Age of Great Peace, the Age of Great Harmony in the Book of Rites, Sun Yat-sen's stage of democracy, and what Western scholars call socialist society are all waiting for us.

Inaugural Message 202

— Zhou Shoujuan

The Women's Special Edition, after two months of preparation, finally meets its readers today. I regret not being a daughter myself, and I do not have a deep understanding of women's issues. Therefore, this publication does not dare to take on the mission of guiding the women's community, but only from a male perspective to conduct in-depth research with the sisters and hope to gradually improve the status of women in the future and overthrow the inherited concept of valuing men over women.

Since the German dictator Hitler chanted the tune of "women returning to the family," a storm of criticism arose, and the women's community especially opposed it, believing that Hitler had ill intentions. He intended to bury women in the family, so they would have no right to ask about social and national affairs, so that men could control everything and do whatever they wanted.

The dictator's claims, of course, inevitably contain selfish and self-serving prejudices, which are absolutely unacceptable. In the editor's view, women's comings and goings must still adopt a compromise method, that is, when society and the country have events, they should stand up and directly serve society and the country, and when society and the country have nothing to do, then they may as well retreat to the family and be their virtuous wives and good mothers.

The sisters should not think that the scope of the family is too narrow and the tasks are too trivial to bother with personally. The ancients said that to govern a country, one must first manage one's family, and only when the family is managed well can the country be governed. This is indeed true. Serving the family is no less important than serving society and the country. For example, if a housewife is not at home all day, entrusts her children to a nanny for education, and leaves the housework to the maids, the result will certainly not be good. When children first open their minds, they develop all kinds of bad habits, which have a major impact on society and the country. If housework is not personally attended to and the maids act recklessly, it will inevitably lead to chaos and even countless problems, causing the husband to always have concerns and be unable to concentrate on serving society and the country. Therefore, I believe that women cannot leave the family, and the family really needs a virtuous wife and good mother.

If women think that the affairs in the family are too simple and do not take much time, then they can engage in academic research in their spare time. Madame Curie of France, who invented radium and benefited the world, is the best example. Those who have the ambition should do the same. May everyone work together!

Symposium

Thoughts on the Shenbao's Launch of the "Women's Special Edition" 203

— Zhan Zhan

The Shenbao's special "Women's Special Edition" every Saturday, starting in the 25th year, shows the thoughtfulness of the newspaper's colleagues. This women's issue, which once attracted attention, but now even women themselves do not pay attention to it, is brought up again by the newspaper to shift the eyes of the social community. From the perspective of women, this cannot be described as a very gratifying thing!

Many people say that men and women now stand on an equal footing, and women do not have any special problems. If there are problems, they are various problems shared by men and women—such as vocational education, economics, etc.—rather than problems unique to women. Women have problems only under very special circumstances. Talking about women's issues now seems to be like yesterday's news.

At first glance, it seems that women have no special problems for discussion. Upon careful consideration, we realize that women's personal problems are still numerous! Not only do women have many problems under special circumstances, but even if men and women are completely equal, women's problems still exist—and will always exist.

A woman can be equal to a man in law, economics, education, and politics, but a woman herself still has her special tasks. Are the responsibilities of being a mother and a wife completely consistent with the responsibilities of being a father and a husband? Therefore, there are many problems that mothers and wives should pay attention to. In terms of the actual situation, the living conditions of most women in China today, whether they are intellectuals or ignorant women, are different from those of general men. Their scope is mostly limited to the family; their duties are mostly managing the household and raising children. Since the facts are so, we absolutely cannot ignore the facts and sing high-pitched tunes. To improve the efficiency of their lives, women's specialized publications have their special value.

As for whether men and women in our country today—and even in the whole world—are completely standing on an equal footing, this is something that everyone knows is not true. At most, we can say that some people are opposing gender equality. In terms of the actual situation, this world is still a world ruled by men, which everyone must also admit. Women in this position have even more problems. The launch of the "Women's Special Edition" not only allows mothers and wives to use it as a mouthpiece to express their grievances. Women's problems in the family and in society can all be published and discussed in its pages. If it can do this, the "Women's Special Edition" will have its actual contribution.

Special Report

Impressions of Nie Zeng Jifen 204

— Huang Jiping

After the publication plan of this journal was determined, we carried out two things: one was to specially invite female pioneers to write articles, and the other was to collect materials on women's issues. I really want to expand this garden, so that the domestic women's community has the opportunity to discuss together; however, I dare not predict whether our wish can be effectively achieved. If the women's community can work together, this small wish may not become an illusion. As for myself, I plan to spend part of my time every week to visit female leaders, record their great theories as a guideline, and I hope readers will correct any omissions!

In Shanghai, female talents emerge in large numbers, and there are countless people who can express opinions and write articles. However, those who combine wisdom and virtue and are known for promoting mother education are not easy to find. After thinking about it, the first person I thought of was Mrs. Nie—Zeng Jifen. She is the daughter of Zeng Wenzheng Gong and the mother of Mr. Nie Yuntai. She is 85 years old this year. She has been diligent and thrifty in managing her family and has worked hard in family education throughout her life. To say that she is a true virtuous wife and good mother, she can be called the first person of the contemporary era!

The time I visited Mrs. Nie was on the morning of January 9th. When I walked into Chongde Hall on Liaoyang Road, the Western-style building was silent. Mr. Yuntai was chanting scriptures in the Buddhist hall. The family led me to the living room to wait. I saw three portraits hanging on the wall. On the left and right were Zeng Wenzheng Gong and his wife, and the other was Mrs. Nie. After a while, Mr. Yuntai invited me into his study. He was very humble and had the demeanor of a gentleman. He spoke Hunan dialect and did not forget his roots. In my previous imagination, Mr. Yuntai was a tycoon in the industrial world. Who knew that after talking to him, I realized that he was also knowledgeable and had outstanding academic skills? In recent years, he has closed his doors to guests and has been studying ancient and modern books without omission. So, we started talking about ancient Chinese culture and went all the way to Western culture, the Meiji Restoration of Japan, the political situation in the Soviet Union, and Chinese women. Once he started talking, he was eloquent, and the problems became bigger and bigger, farther and farther away from what I wanted to ask. In the end, he praised Mr. Liang Shuming to the highest degree, and regarded Liang's book "The Last Awakening in the Chinese National Salvation Movement" as a masterpiece that young people must read. Two hours passed in a flash, and I said that I wanted to talk about the topic now and asked him to introduce me to the old lady, so we slowly went upstairs.

The Chongde old man came out very briskly, with a kind and benevolent smile that made people respectful. She was healthy and looked like she was in her 60s. To save the old lady's time, I didn't dare to talk too much and only asked the following questions:

How has the old lady managed the family for sixty years?

I have always followed the principles of integrity, diligence, thrift, and peace to guide my children. Everyone is united in mind and heart, helping and encouraging each other, so there has never been idle talk in the family, and the children and grandchildren have been able to work hard and make progress. Even now, they still do not change their original aspirations. According to my experience, as long as the parents can respect etiquette and morality, family education will not be decadent. (Mr. Yuntai said: My mother has a gentle and kind nature and has never spoken harshly, so her words are always happily followed by her children and grandchildren.)

What are the old lady's opinions on the small family and the large family system?

I think each has its advantages and disadvantages. According to the current trend, large families have no possibility of existence. Even my family has adopted the small family system, but they are interconnected and closely related, and still do not lose the fun of the large family. In general, the biggest shortcoming of small families is that they do not care about the support of the elders. Let me tell you a few facts: a senior official of the Customs has a monthly salary of 800, and his father is a tax officer. His mother is old, and neither father nor son cares about her. The mother borrows ten or eight yuan from her son, and he always acts high and mighty. This is one thing. An old beggar went to a mansion to beg, and the owner took out one yuan and threw it out the window. The old beggar took the silver and left in tears. People asked him why he only got one yuan. He said, "This is my son's villa!" This is another thing. A celebrity at sea owns huge sums of money, but his father is still driving a horse-drawn carriage on the streets of New York. Do you think these things are reasonable?

Picture of Teaching Children Arithmetic 205

I heard that your house used to publish a family quarterly and hold family gatherings. Please tell me about the process.

This is a thing of the past. Because our family of more than 80 people was scattered in all directions, it was not easy to gather them together. So, my son Yuntai edited the "Nie Family Quarterly", which was later changed to a quarterly. Family members freely expressed their opinions. In five or six years, the circulation increased from more than one hundred copies to more than three thousand copies. At first, it was only for family members to read, but later, relatives and friends asked to read it, and even provinces, cities, and counties came to read it. A collection was published every year, for a total of five or six collections. Seven or eight years ago, Yuntai became ill, and the family newspaper stopped publishing. At that time, the "Nie Family Benefit Meeting" was held every Sunday, and young and old gathered together. It was a grand event. Each record was also specially published in a small booklet to show that it was not forgotten.

How does the old lady spend her time now?

I don't often sit in a carriage and go to the streets to see the market, select and make various medicinal pills, or distribute money to help the poor and sick, to fulfill my wishes. Besides, there is nothing else. At this time, it was already noon, so I said goodbye and left.

Working Women in Rural Areas 206

— Gui Chui

On Chinese Women Studying in Japan 207

— Yi Fa

When the Japanese currency fell last year, many female students took this opportunity to study in Japan. Now, although the price of Chinese and Japanese currencies is almost equal, there are still many female students coming to Japan to study. The educational purpose of Japanese women is completely different from that of men, so most girls' schools only offer courses such as housekeeping and sewing. Ordinary women graduate from junior high school and higher girls' school. Not many enter women's universities or take university education with men. Among the Chinese female students studying in Japan, most study medicine. They enter specialized schools of obstetrics, dentistry, and ophthalmology. Others enter various private universities to study liberal arts, law, and economics. Very few study education, agriculture, and industry.

Because female students who come to study in Japan mostly want to enter schools above the specialized level, they must obtain a high school diploma or above in China before they can enter school. Although Japanese private schools often enroll Chinese students without exams, there are also schools with extremely difficult entrance exams. Chinese female students hear in China that it is easy to enter Japanese schools, so some come to Japan without a certificate, and as a result, they often fall into a dilemma.

The social interaction between Chinese male and female students has always been open. Especially female students studying in Japan, because they live in a foreign country and have no relatives, they must have a few boyfriends to take care of each other. However, in Japan, where the old etiquette is extremely important, there is often suspicion about the interaction between female students studying in Japan and their boyfriends. And inevitably, a few female students neglect their studies because they are pursued by male students, which is very regrettable. In fact, male students living alone in a foreign country have to do the work of tidying up their rooms and mending their clothes and socks themselves. However, female students often refuse to do such trivial things and hire Japanese maids to serve them. Therefore, the Japanese mistakenly believe that all Chinese women are like female students studying abroad who are unwilling to manage housework. On the one hand, it makes Japanese women even more hardworking in managing the family.

Chinese students studying abroad always wear student uniforms and Western suits all year round. Even if someone brings a few pieces of Chinese clothing and suddenly wears them, they are often ridiculed by their peers. This is a special mentality. However, Westerners and Japanese who come to our inland areas have never been seen wearing Chinese long robes and short jackets. So, if you ask why students studying abroad don't wear Chinese clothes, no one can answer. The only exception is female students studying in Japan. Except for sometimes wearing Japanese clothes for fun out of curiosity, they all wear cheongsams, just like in China. This is admirable. They still preserve the essence of our country.

In China, female students already have the phenomenon of being well cared for and disdainful of handling housework. Since studying abroad, this mentality may be even more advanced. They often despise Japanese women for being willing to be slaves and taking pride in serving men. On the one hand, they observe the diligence of Japanese women in housework and the harmonious relationship between couples, and they cannot help but admire them. Therefore, the observation of Japanese women by Chinese female students studying in Japan is in a relative state.

We often see groups of Japanese women crossing the ocean to marry overseas residents or marry local natives in various places. Sometimes, forced by life, they follow men to cultivate abroad. It is not uncommon for Japanese people to be respected for going to study abroad far away from their motherland for the sake of learning.

Drifting (Part 1) 208

— Qin Wang Yin Jiu

This is really a terribly frightening story. Although there was no bombing by planes or tigers eating people and other bloody deeds, I can't help but feel my heart beat faster and feel infinite sadness when I think about it; because the victim in this incident—Sister Qiuyun—still doesn't know where she is drifting to this day!

Sister Qiuyun was originally the happiest one among our classmates. She had beauty, health, and intelligence endowed by heaven, which were several points better than others; we often had to suspect that heaven was favoring her in the same way as Mrs. Nuttall in school, otherwise, how could her academic performance be so good, and her body be so excellent? What was especially enviable was that she also had a very happy family: her father was not a high official, but because he had been working in the banking industry for a long time, his position was quite high, and his economy was relatively affluent, but he was not a big banker with hundreds of thousands or millions of assets, so there was no need to worry about kidnapping; her mother was a veteran normal school graduate, and of course her temperament was extremely kind and her mind was also very modern; she had three elder brothers, the first and second of whom already had considerable occupations, and the third was still studying, and they were all very friendly to her; and in terms of her parents, because they had three boys first before they got her, this girl, they loved her even more than the three elder brothers. She grew up gradually in this satisfying environment, as carefree and comfortable as a swan. In school, she was even praised by the teachers, and in terms of classmates, even if she seemed a little proud, and inevitably a part of the people were hostile to her, these irrelevant obstacles would never affect her beautiful life. She finally graduated very happily from the university department, and also received the first-place A-level honor award. When we shook hands and said goodbye at the door of the auditorium, she carried a flower basket given to her by her cousin and said to me with a smile:

It turned out that her father deeply loved this only daughter. A month before she graduated, he had already prepared the procedures for her to study abroad. She herself was of course very excited and would tell everyone she met about this.

Standard Woman - The Simple Life of the Blackshirt Prime Minister's Wife 209

— Special Correspondent

She could live in a grand official residence, but she prefers to live in a simple country home.

She could hire a throng of servants and live a life of ease and luxury, but she enjoys handling all the household affairs herself, even going into the kitchen to cook. She could socialize with the nobles of the court, but she prefers to chat with ordinary people.

If others were in her position, they would certainly be arrogant and condescending, but she remains kind and approachable, never putting on airs of a noble lady.

Who is this noble lady? It is none other than Mrs. Rachele, the wife of the world-famous Italian dictator, the Blackshirt Prime Minister Benito Mussolini.

Mussolini is currently devoting all his efforts to the war with Abyssinia. If the Italian army can achieve a great victory in this war, forcing Abyssinia to cede vast territories and join the Italian domain, then Mussolini's position will be more secure than ever, and he will become an idol worshipped by the Italian people. If the war drags on with no end in sight, with the soldiers' blood constantly staining the battlefields and the treasury's gold continuously being sent abroad, once panic breaks out at home, Mussolini's authority may inevitably fall. Mussolini's eldest son, Bruno, and his second son, Vittorio, are currently serving in the air force on the front lines in Abyssinia. His son-in-law, Count Ciano, is also the commander of the air force's suicide squad.

The entire Italian people are willing to express their patriotic fervor for the Italian-Abyssinian war, and they are all extremely concerned about the war's outcome. But no one is more concerned than Mussolini's wife, Rachele, because her husband's lifelong happiness and the lives of her two sons and one son-in-law are all closely related to the war. Although she is worried sick, she keeps it hidden in her heart, unwilling to show the world even a hint of it. Her daily life remains unchanged. Born into humble circumstances, she never harbored any desires for a life of ease and luxury. She avoids all social engagements and never attends any grand ceremonies. She does not seek to share in her husband's glory. She lived in an ordinary house in Milan for a long time, and now, she still spends most of the year in seclusion in the countryside.

She avoids public attention and seeks to enjoy family life out of her own nature, not out of any compulsion. But even if she wanted to change her situation, she would not have the opportunity, because Mussolini has always maintained that women's place is in the home, which is praised by Italy and the world.

Mrs. Mussolini also has several other distinctive traits. She prefers choosing plump young chickens to understanding national politics. She is better at cooking delicious fish dishes than at socializing at receptions. She loves listening to her children's babbling more than engaging in social chit-chat. She disdains all fashionable clothes, expensive jewelry, and other luxuries.

If Mussolini were to lose power and step down tomorrow, becoming a poor man again, his wife would be able to live with him peacefully in the same simple, frugal life they had many years ago when they were young and poor, without feeling any pain. If she were to sigh at that time, it would certainly not be because her good dreams had been shattered, but only because her husband's grand ambition to make Italy an unsurpassed power had failed midway. It can be asserted that her wish is only to live with her husband and children in an ordinary house, enjoying the joy of family life. At that time, she will truly become that kind of woman.

In short, Rachele, as the prime minister's wife, could well have lived a life of ease and luxury and shown off her status to the public, enjoying the flattery of the masses. Although her husband advocates that women's place is in the home, she could still do as she pleases. But now, she hides in the countryside, personally grinding grain and still retaining the flavor of a country woman. In the eyes of the average modern official's wife, she is simply a foolish woman. However, who praises the cleverness of modern officials' wives?

Shanghai Local Supplement

Commentary

Chinese Cinema and "Extraordinary Times" in 1936 221

— Lv Gang

This is not an arbitrary assertion, nor a prediction, but an observation based on the development of the current situation. 1936 will be an "extraordinary time." Following 1935, in a world full of crises, it will be even more dangerous and turbulent. Although 1935 was spent amidst dense war clouds and numerous wounds, it is difficult for us to say, at the beginning of this new year, whether 1936 can pass through this great difficulty unscathed. Looking back, in the recently passed 1935, East Africa, following the Far East, also experienced a war of imperialist aggression against a semi-colonial country. The only difference is that the former's government, under the urging of the people, rose up to resist, while the latter, in order to maintain peace, repeatedly lost provinces covering millions of square kilometers. However, the two are the same in that the imperialists, in the midst of urgent crises, plunder the interests of weak nations in order to seek their own way out.

During the September 18th Incident, China's cinema was stimulated by the situation, and both its quality and quantity were greatly improved. The selection of themes no longer followed the previous feudal-style chivalrous stories and absurd low-level novels. Many films with the theme of anti-imperialist national war appeared on the market. Moreover, the improvement of Chinese film production technology also took this period as a major turning point. But in reality, it was ultimately a manifestation of the Chinese people's rising emotions for national independence and liberation. Because we cannot deny that cinema, like drama, is a tool of education and a weapon of combat. Therefore, the Chinese people's support for the appearance of films with anti-imperialist themes, which influenced general film practitioners to compete in producing such films, was not accidental. However, as the situation changed, the anti-imperialist climax declined due to environmental obstacles. Speculative film practitioners then turned to producing films far removed from reality, and some even moved women's legs to the screen, pursuing their sweet, intoxicating, and rosy dreams. However, in these past two years, China's crisis has deepened compared to the era of the September 18th Incident, and the enemy has taken advantage of the danger to repeatedly occupy North China to complete its daydream of a continental policy. Yet, film authors do not seize on this current theme, but instead delve into the path of decadence, attempting to indirectly anesthetize the nerves of the people for the enemy. How tragic is this!

Now, we have entered the "extraordinary time" of 1936. The crisis will only increase compared to the previous year. With countless difficulties ahead, where will Chinese cinema go? Is it still good to be in a cloudy world, forging beautiful dreams under the enemy's gunfire? I think that even if the masses do not explicitly express their new demands for film themes, in the current situation, film authors should also deeply reflect on themselves. Naturally, there were progressive films last year, but compared to the total number of films, the difference is too great.

Opening up the era of 1936, this eventful autumn of "extraordinary times," in order to save ourselves and to save this world that is about to be split and destroyed by imperialism, we must also showcase Chinese cinema and see how it will reflect this turbulent year.

At that time, Zhuanxu and his followers chased to the broken part of Buzhou Mountain, saw the party of Gonggong scattered there, and shouted and killed. Gonggong also gathered his party and made a life-and-death battle with Zhuanxu. For a time, the noise shook the sky, and blood flowed everywhere. (19)

Bridge 223

— Family Member

There is a long, wooden plank bridge that connects the town and the village. It is important, like the bones of the human body. With it, a bridge, people on both ends begin to come and go frequently. Thinking back to the time before the bridge, although there were boatmen who could replace the bridge, carrying people on both ends, it always took too much time and manpower.

Because both sides felt its need, two sharp-tongued individuals took the lead, soliciting donations from the rich and apportioning contributions to shopkeepers. ... The resulting amount is a mystery! But it must have been a large sum.

So the bridge was built, but it was so crude:

Driving a few wooden piles into the riverbed, placing a few horizontal timbers on the piles, and laying three large planks, nailing them firmly with iron nails. A bridge was completed. Two months of work was not even enough. As for the railings on both sides of the bridge, they were simply made of weak bamboo poles. People walking across the bridge couldn't even rest their arms on them before the railings swayed and vibrated.

However, there was finally such a bridge for people to use, and a new, happy feeling would float into people's minds.

—Like hanging in mid-air without touching the ground. How dangerous!

But then some people had thoughts like this come to mind. Because when walking on it, the wooden planks rustled, as if they would fall down at any moment. And from under the bridge, sitting on a boat and looking up, looking at the middle of the piles connecting to each other, because when the river water rose, it was impacted by the water force, again and again, the connecting position gradually moved away, as if it were just placed there. People walking on the bridge, moving and moving, it would collapse, almost making people feel a terrible premonition at any time.

And the people who pass by on the bridge every day are bustling and countless.

One day there will be trouble, and the people on the boats coming and going under the bridge will often worry about the people on the bridge.

Spring rains are especially heavy, often raining continuously for days, so the river water rises, and the water slowly surges upwards, with the water level almost level with the bridge bank. One can reach out and dip into the water, and the wooden piles are submerged in the water and cannot be seen. Thus, the bridge seems even more like it is floating on the water.

And in the spring, on this end of the bridge is the city, and on the other end is the village area. As usual, every spring is the grand season for holding dragon boat races. Because there is that bridge, people standing on the bridge can get a good view, so the location was changed from another place to here, to that side of the bridge.

That afternoon, there were countless people who came to the bridge from both sides, from the village and from the city, to attend the event. The railings on both sides of the bridge were crowded with people from beginning to end. The dragon boats sped on the turbulent waves, one against the other, beating drums and gongs, competing with each other. Countless people on the bridge clapped and shouted at the top of their lungs when they were happy, cheering them on. Some people were pushed to the back and couldn't see clearly, so they pushed forward hard, and the people in front pushed back, everyone forgetting that they were standing on a bridge that seemed to be floating on the water. As a result of pushing back and forth, starting from the railings that were pushed broken, the rest of the railings all collapsed together, and then people rolled into the water one by one. And the river under the bridge was turbulent and bottomless, those who rolled in were immediately swept into the roaring whirlpool and sank; perished.

Those who did not roll down, seeing their companions swallowed by the waves, a great cry filled the space.

It also became a great ritual for the dragon boat race.

That incident was three months after the bridge was completed. Who should be blamed for this? Perhaps only the ignorant bridge, and the ignorant curses of the people.

And then, the rain continued to pour down heavily, endlessly for ten days or half a month, the river water rose step by step, even submerging the entire bridge in the thick, turbid yellow water. Finally, the city gates also lowered the water gates, and the boatmen also sailed to the riverbank and tied a thick rope to the large bridge trunk on the shore, securing it tightly, so the people on both ends had to temporarily sever relations. Separated by a vast expanse of water. After some days passed, the rain stopped, and the river water gradually receded, but the bridge was almost completely destroyed. And a bridge is indispensable, naturally important to build, but this time, because of the lesson of the previous dragon boat race tragedy, everyone felt the need to demand permanent safety, it is best to use cement and steel bars to cast it, but it requires a very large construction fee...

Large-scale fundraising and apportionment began.

Several months passed, and it was said that the harvest was satisfactory, and the people on both ends were unusually excited and happy. The construction of the new bridge also started. Soon after, the new bridge was completed. But it was still exactly the same as the old bridge, crude. The only difference was that it was slightly wider.

People were disappointed: There was money to build a bridge with cement and steel bars, why is it still a makeshift wooden bridge?

The money for building the bridge was collected by everyone. In the past, although it was very difficult to travel back and forth without a bridge, there was no unexpected burden of repairing and building the bridge. But now, there is a bridge, and at the same time, there is an unexpected and almost compulsory apportionment. As for a safe bridge, it has never been produced. Seeing that bridge, people can't help but be angry and surprised.

Hua Mei (1060) 1 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Peach Blossom Spring"

Where is the immortal source to avoid the Qin? In the past, a Wuling man explored the secluded place. He, fishing for a living, was leisurely and carefree. He often traveled on the misty waves. He forgot how far he had gone, only caring to go forward along the stream. Suddenly, he saw peach blossoms on both banks, redder than brocade. Fragrant grass filled the embankment, greener than turf. At the end of the forest, a beautiful mountain rose up in front of him. Then the cave entrance revealed light. The fisherman, leaving his boat and going ashore, entered. He walked through the peach blossoms and saw a village. Fields and paths intersected, with lush mulberry trees and bamboo. The crowing of chickens and barking of dogs could be heard in the distance. The men and women in the fields wore ancient clothes. Suddenly, they met and greeted each other with smiles. The elderly and the young were all joyful. They killed chickens and made food to feast the guests. They said that their ancestors had come here to escape the chaos of the Qin Dynasty. They had come to this isolated place to live. Today, they did not know what world it was, as if they were cut off from the mundane world. The fisherman fully described the events of the present day. They sighed together about the changes in the world. They prepared wine and food and invited him to stay. They treated him warmly and earnestly. The fisherman lingered for several days before returning. They all said, "Do not tell the outside world about this encounter." The fisherman returned to his boat and marked the original road. He told the governor of the county when he arrived at the shore. The governor sent people to follow him to explore again. The entrance of the cave was lost in the mist and could not be found. The noble scholar Liu Ziji of Nanyang went there in person with joy, but it was also in vain. From then on, no one asked about it again.

Xia Hesheng's Three Smiles

Dun Ben (800) 7 PM to 8 PM

Opening Thought

Changchun has beautiful scenery. Peach and plum blossoms compete in beauty and are especially fragrant. The peony, the color of the country, blooms with wealth and honor. They compete with the herbs and gather fragrance. Thousands of reds and purples welcome the spring. They attract butterflies to fly around busily. The cuckoo on the branch does not stop singing. It teaches me to be lazy to dress up in front of the mirror. The cherries unintentionally dot rouge. The dejected hibiscus has long green eyebrows. The spring silk clothes have not been changed. The light skirt is tied with fluttering ribbons. The double lotus is noble. Who will paint it? Suddenly, I stop embroidering, thinking of you. I secretly divine under the lamp. Every night my soul crosses the ocean in dreams. After the cold plum is separated from the clouds, the moment passes and the begonias are released to the sea. The weaver girl and the cowherd are separated by the Silver River. It is difficult to send red beans to the heart. My confidante is a small clove. She smiles and advises me to put on makeup. I only hope that he will achieve fame early and fulfill his ambition. Returning home for farming, we will reunite on the bed of joy. At that time, the sea beauty will often accompany the crape myrtle man.

Du Wenkui, Zhou Jianhong, Big Red Robe

Zhong Xi (1040) 12:15 AM to 1 AM

Opening "Guan Shoufeng's Restaurant Asks for a Team"

The old hero is the frugal retail merchant. It is Guan Shoufeng, with white hair and a wrinkled face. Only to see soldiers escort him in a motorcycle. Unexpectedly, his daughter has returned home gloriously. That Xiugu, smiling and carrying a bag in both hands, enters. She tells the twists and turns of the situation in detail. Shoufeng, listening, is secretly pleased in his heart. He is worthy of being a Huangshan knight. Xiugu is majestic. What a magnificent sight. It is very different from before. She is only saying goodbye to her neighbors in the same courtyard.

Said that I have entrusted my life to a red silk. Today I am leaving Beijing with a lost expression. That is why I am not waiting to say goodbye. Those neighbors in the same courtyard are all surprised to see her. They envy her for entering the clouds and rising to the ninth heaven. Waiting to see the girl's car driving away. Shoufeng smiles calmly and is filled with joy. I really can't bear to let my daughter go. It is only because the road is long and there are thousands of miles of mountains. I don't know when we will meet again. That is why I am sending a flying wild goose with a long gaze. Although I have been living with you day and night for a long time, I can only say goodbye to you like parting swallows. I will entrust you with the silver money cloth bag. This trip is all said in silence. Furthermore, the Fan family's son and the old man have agreed to be companions in the restaurant today. It is nothing more than a temporary farewell to talk about old times. It is good that I have no companions to wander around the world. I am only used to walking east and west with my daughter. Today I advise you to drink one more cup of wine. It is only because the beauty is suffering from a disease of infatuation. You must never mention the old things and keep her in your heart.

Movie

A Brief Discussion of "Wild Geese Descending on the Cold River" 229

From the completion of "Pear Blossoms in the Rain" to "Wild Geese Descending on the Cold River"

About two years have passed between them, and director Ma Xubang has spent all this time on the preparation of the script, and the preparation and production work. Moreover, this script was specially written for Chen Yanyan. If we say that it is an exceptionally excellent work, you will not disbelieve it.

This amazing work of art

It has a lively and strong life. You say it is like a fragrant and rich flower; but it is also like a raging fire of struggle burning in the hearts of every young person.

The poison of feudal remnants still hovers in the human world like a man-eating beast. Here, it has clearly told us how modern young people who have been harmed can eliminate the poison and obtain happiness in life!

This should be said to be a world-class tragedy

Because its plot is tortuous and moving, its depiction is detailed, and its style is fresh and beautiful; therefore, watching this film is like reading a novel with great literary value. We dare to guarantee this.

Comparison of Ancient and Modern Song of Everlasting Regret 232

One is a poet and the other is an artist. Shi Dongshan is not inferior to Bai Xiangshan

Bai Juyi of the Tang Dynasty once wrote the Song of Everlasting Regret, praising the Tang Emperor's love for his concubine, Yang Guifei. The entanglement and sadness caused many sentimental people in the world to read it and shed tears. However, in the lines, there was quite a bit of sarcasm towards the Tang Emperor for valuing women and neglecting the country. Director Shi Dongshan wrote and directed the Song of Everlasting Regret for Xinhua, describing how aspiring young people in modern society work hard for their lives and have no time to offer hospitality to their bedside companions, causing misunderstandings and creating great tragedies. Although its meaning is very different from Bai Juyi's Song of Everlasting Regret, the tragedy and hatred are the same, just like what Bai Juyi said, "Heaven and earth will eventually come to an end, but this hatred will last forever!" Moreover, Director Shi satirizes the sinister and treacherous nature of people in industry and commerce, jealousy and competition; they do not know how to close their own doors and create their own unique style. They only know how to imitate and compete to lower prices and sell cheaply, disregarding costs and credit. As a result, the entire industry and commerce falls to the ground and cannot be recovered. Director Shi has such awareness and also adopts the romance of ancient stories to form this great tragedy. The protagonist Wang Renmei sings the Song of Everlasting Regret in the film with a desperate and moving voice, even better than Fishing Light Serenade.
